<p><b>Sir James Paul McCartney</b> <span style="font-size:100%;"><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Member_of_the_Order_of_the_British_Empire" title="Member of the Order of the British Empire">MBE</a></span> (born 18 June 1942) is an English singer, multi-instrumentalist, and composer. With <a href="/wiki/John_Lennon" title="John Lennon">John Lennon</a>, <a href="/wiki/George_Harrison" title="George Harrison">George Harrison</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Ringo_Starr" title="Ringo Starr">Ringo Starr</a>, he gained worldwide fame as a member of <a href="/wiki/The_Beatles" title="The Beatles">the Beatles</a>, one of the most popular and influential acts in the history of rock music; his <a href="/wiki/Lennon%E2%80%93McCartney" title="Lennon–McCartney">songwriting partnership with Lennon</a> is one of the most celebrated of the 20th century. After <a href="/wiki/Break-up_of_the_Beatles" title="Break-up of the Beatles">the band's break-up</a>, he pursued a solo career and formed <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Wings_(band)" title="Wings (band)">Wings</a> with his first wife, <a href="/wiki/Linda_McCartney" title="Linda McCartney">Linda</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Denny_Laine" title="Denny Laine">Denny Laine</a>.</p>
<p>McCartney has been recognised as one of the most successful composers and performers of all time, with 60 <a href="/wiki/Music_recording_sales_certification" title="Music recording sales certification">gold discs</a> and sales of over 100 million albums and 100 million singles of his work with the Beatles and as a solo artist.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2"><a href="#cite_note-2"><span>[</span>2<span>]</span></a></sup> More than 2,200 artists have covered his Beatles song "<a href="/wiki/Yesterday_(Beatles_song)" title="Yesterday (Beatles song)">Yesterday</a>", more than any other copyrighted song in history. Wings' 1977 release "<a href="/wiki/Mull_of_Kintyre_(song)" title="Mull of Kintyre (song)">Mull of Kintyre</a>" is one of the all-time best-selling singles in the UK. <a href="/wiki/List_of_Rock_and_Roll_Hall_of_Fame_inductees#Performers" title="List of Rock and Roll Hall of Fame inductees">Inducted</a> into the <a href="/wiki/Rock_and_Roll_Hall_of_Fame" title="Rock and Roll Hall of Fame">Rock and Roll Hall of Fame</a> as a solo artist in March 1999, McCartney has written, or co-written 32 songs that have reached number one on the <a href="/wiki/Billboard_Hot_100" title="Billboard Hot 100"><i>Billboard</i> Hot 100</a>, and as of 2014<sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Paul_McCartney&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup> he has sold more than 15.5 million <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/RIAA" title="RIAA">RIAA</a>-certified units in the United States. McCartney, Lennon, Harrison and Starr received MBEs in 1965, and in 1997, McCartney was <a href="/wiki/Knight_Bachelor" title="Knight Bachelor">knighted</a> for his services to music.</p>
<p>McCartney has released an extensive catalogue of songs as a solo artist and has composed classical and electronic music. He has taken part in projects to promote international charities related to such subjects as <a href="/wiki/Animal_rights" title="Animal rights">animal rights</a>, <a href="/wiki/Seal_hunting" title="Seal hunting">seal hunting</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Land_mines" title="Land mines">land mines</a>, vegetarianism, poverty, and <a href="/wiki/Music_education" title="Music education">music education</a>. He has married three times and is the father of five children.</p>

<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-42"><a href="#Discography"><span class="tocnumber">7</span> <span class="toctext">Discography</span></a></li>
<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-43"><a href="#Tours"><span class="tocnumber">8</span> <span class="toctext">Tours</span></a></li>
<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-44"><a href="#See_also"><span class="tocnumber">9</span> <span class="toctext">See also</span></a></li>
<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-45"><a href="#Notes"><span class="tocnumber">10</span> <span class="toctext">Notes</span></a></li>
<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-46"><a href="#Citations"><span class="tocnumber">11</span> <span class="toctext">Citations</span></a></li>
<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-47"><a href="#Sources"><span class="tocnumber">12</span> <span class="toctext">Sources</span></a></li>
<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-48"><a href="#Further_reading"><span class="tocnumber">13</span> <span class="toctext">Further reading</span></a></li>

</ul>
</div>
</div>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Childhood">Childhood</span></h2>
<div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Jim_and_Mary_McCartney" title="Jim and Mary McCartney">Jim and Mary McCartney</a></div>
<p>James Paul McCartney was born on 18 June 1942, in <a href="/wiki/Walton,_Liverpool" title="Walton, Liverpool">Walton Hospital</a>, Liverpool, England, where his mother, Mary (née Mohin), had qualified to practise as a nurse. His father, James ("Jim") McCartney, was absent from his son's birth due to his work as a volunteer firefighter during World War II.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESpitz200575_3-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESpitz200575-3"><span>[</span>3<span>]</span></a></sup> Paul has one younger brother, <a href="/wiki/Mike_McGear" title="Mike McGear">Michael</a> (born 7 January 1944). Though the children were baptised in their mother's Catholic faith, because their father was a former Protestant turned agnostic, religion was not emphasised in the household.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-4"><a href="#cite_note-4"><span>[</span>4<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>McCartney had attended Stockton Wood Road Primary School from 1947 until 1949, when he transferred to Joseph Williams Junior School due to overcrowding at Stockton.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-5"><a href="#cite_note-5"><span>[</span>5<span>]</span></a></sup> In 1953, he passed the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/11-plus" title="11-plus">11-plus</a> exam, with only three others out of ninety examinees, gaining admission to the <a href="/wiki/Liverpool_Institute_High_School_for_Boys" title="Liverpool Institute High School for Boys">Liverpool Institute</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-6"><a href="#cite_note-6"><span>[</span>6<span>]</span></a></sup> In 1954, he met schoolmate <a href="/wiki/George_Harrison" title="George Harrison">George Harrison</a> on the bus to the Institute from his suburban home in <a href="/wiki/Speke" title="Speke">Speke</a>. Harrison had also passed the exam, meaning he could attend a <a href="/wiki/Grammar_school" title="Grammar school">grammar school</a> rather than a <a href="/wiki/Secondary_modern_school" title="Secondary modern school">secondary modern school</a>, where most pupils went until becoming eligible for work. The two quickly became friends; McCartney later admitted: "I tended to talk down to him because he was a year younger."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-7"><a href="#cite_note-7"><span>[</span>7<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:20_forthlin_road.jpg"><img alt="Exterior of a two-story brick building, with a hedge in front of it. Six windows are visible, three on each level, as are two doorways on the lower level." class="thumbimage" data-file-height="585" data-file-width="772" height="167" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/43/20_forthlin_road.jpg/220px-20_forthlin_road.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/43/20_forthlin_road.jpg/330px-20_forthlin_road.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/43/20_forthlin_road.jpg/440px-20_forthlin_road.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:20_forthlin_road.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
McCartney's former home, 20 Forthlin Road</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>McCartney's mother Mary was a <a href="/wiki/Midwife" title="Midwife">midwife</a> and the family's primary wage earner, enabling them to move into <a href="/wiki/20_Forthlin_Road" title="20 Forthlin Road">20 Forthlin Road</a> in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Allerton,_Merseyside" title="Allerton, Merseyside">Allerton</a>, where they lived until 1964.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-8"><a href="#cite_note-8"><span>[</span>8<span>]</span></a></sup> She rode a bicycle to her patients; McCartney described an early memory of her leaving at "about three in the morning [the] streets ... thick with snow".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMiles19976_9-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMiles19976-9"><span>[</span>9<span>]</span></a></sup> On 31 October 1956, when McCartney was fourteen, his mother died of an <a href="/wiki/Embolism" title="Embolism">embolism</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10"><a href="#cite_note-10"><span>[</span>10<span>]</span></a></sup> McCartney's loss later became a point of connection with <a href="/wiki/John_Lennon" title="John Lennon">John Lennon</a>, whose mother, <a href="/wiki/Julia_Lennon" title="Julia Lennon">Julia</a>, had died when he was seventeen.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMiles199731_11-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMiles199731-11"><span>[</span>11<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>McCartney's father was a trumpet player and pianist who led Jim Mac's Jazz Band in the 1920s. He kept an <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Upright_piano" title="Upright piano">upright piano</a> in the front room, encouraged his sons to be musical and advised Paul to take piano lessons, but he preferred to learn <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Learning_music_by_ear" title="Learning music by ear">by ear</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMiles199722.E2.80.9323_12-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMiles199722.E2.80.9323-12"><span>[</span>12<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-15"><a href="#cite_note-15"><span>[</span>nb 1<span>]</span></a></sup> Jim gave Paul a nickel-plated trumpet for his fourteenth birthday, but when <a href="/wiki/Rock_and_roll" title="Rock and roll">rock and roll</a> became popular on <a href="/wiki/Radio_Luxembourg_(English)" title="Radio Luxembourg (English)">Radio Luxembourg</a>, McCartney traded it for a £15 <a href="/wiki/Framus" title="Framus">Framus</a> Zenith (model 17) <a href="/wiki/Steel-string_acoustic_guitar" title="Steel-string acoustic guitar">acoustic guitar</a>, rationalising that it would be difficult to sing while playing a trumpet.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16"><a href="#cite_note-16"><span>[</span>15<span>]</span></a></sup> He found it difficult to play guitar right-handed, but after noticing a poster advertising a <a href="/wiki/Slim_Whitman" title="Slim Whitman">Slim Whitman</a> concert and realising that Whitman also played left-handed, he reversed the order of the strings.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMiles199721_17-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMiles199721-17"><span>[</span>16<span>]</span></a></sup> McCartney wrote his first song, "<a href="/wiki/I_Lost_My_Little_Girl" title="I Lost My Little Girl">I Lost My Little Girl</a>", on the Zenith, and composed another early tune that would become "<a href="/wiki/When_I%27m_Sixty-Four" title="When I'm Sixty-Four">When I'm Sixty-Four</a>" on the piano. American <a href="/wiki/Rhythm_and_blues" title="Rhythm and blues">rhythm and blues</a> influenced him, and <a href="/wiki/Little_Richard" title="Little Richard">Little Richard</a> was his schoolboy idol; "<a href="/wiki/Long_Tall_Sally" title="Long Tall Sally">Long Tall Sally</a>" was the first song McCartney performed in public, at a <a href="/wiki/Butlins" title="Butlins">Butlins</a> holiday camp talent competition.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-18"><a href="#cite_note-18"><span>[</span>17<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Musical_career">Musical career</span></h2>
<div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Paul_McCartney%27s_musical_career" title="Paul McCartney's musical career">Paul McCartney's musical career</a></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="1957.E2.80.931960:_The_Quarrymen">1957–1960: The Quarrymen</span></h3>
<div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">Main article: <a href="/wiki/The_Quarrymen" title="The Quarrymen">The Quarrymen</a></div>
<p>At the age of fifteen, McCartney met Lennon and his band, the Quarrymen, at the St Peter's Church Hall fête in <a href="/wiki/Woolton" title="Woolton">Woolton</a> on 6 July 1957.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESpitz200593_19-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESpitz200593-19"><span>[</span>18<span>]</span></a></sup> The Quarrymen played a mix of rock and roll and <a href="/wiki/Skiffle" title="Skiffle">skiffle</a>, a type of <a href="/wiki/Popular_music" title="Popular music">popular music</a> with <a href="/wiki/Jazz" title="Jazz">jazz</a>, <a href="/wiki/Blues" title="Blues">blues</a> and <a href="/wiki/Folk_music" title="Folk music">folk</a> influences.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20"><a href="#cite_note-20"><span>[</span>19<span>]</span></a></sup> The band invited McCartney to join soon afterwards as a rhythm guitarist, and he formed a close working relationship with Lennon. Harrison joined in 1958 as lead guitarist, followed by Lennon's art school friend <a href="/wiki/Stuart_Sutcliffe" title="Stuart Sutcliffe">Stuart Sutcliffe</a> on bass, in 1960.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELewisohn199218_21-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELewisohn199218-21"><span>[</span>20<span>]</span></a></sup> By May 1960 the band had tried several names, including <i>Beatals</i>, <i>Johnny and the Moondogs</i> and <i>the Silver Beetles</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELewisohn199218.E2.80.9322_22-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELewisohn199218.E2.80.9322-22"><span>[</span>21<span>]</span></a></sup> They adopted the name <i>the Beatles</i> in August 1960 and recruited drummer <a href="/wiki/Pete_Best" title="Pete Best">Pete Best</a> shortly before a five-engagement residency in <a href="/wiki/Hamburg" title="Hamburg">Hamburg</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELewisohn199217.E2.80.9325_23-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELewisohn199217.E2.80.9325-23"><span>[</span>22<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="1960.E2.80.931970:_The_Beatles">1960–1970: The Beatles</span></h3>
<div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">Main article: <a href="/wiki/The_Beatles" title="The Beatles">The Beatles</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:The_Beatles_in_America.JPG"><img alt="A black-and-white image of Paul McCartney, George Harrison, John Lennon and Ringo Starr waving to fans after arriving in America in 1964. A crowd is visible behind them on the left." class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2526" data-file-width="3578" height="155" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c4/The_Beatles_in_America.JPG/220px-The_Beatles_in_America.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c4/The_Beatles_in_America.JPG/330px-The_Beatles_in_America.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c4/The_Beatles_in_America.JPG/440px-The_Beatles_in_America.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:The_Beatles_in_America.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
McCartney <i>(second from left)</i> with Lennon, Harrison and Starr, 1964</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Informally represented by <a href="/wiki/Allan_Williams" title="Allan Williams">Allan Williams</a>, the Beatles' first booking was for <a href="/wiki/The_Beatles_in_Hamburg" title="The Beatles in Hamburg">a series of performances</a> in Hamburg, starting in 1960.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-24"><a href="#cite_note-24"><span>[</span>23<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-26"><a href="#cite_note-26"><span>[</span>nb 2<span>]</span></a></sup> In 1961, Sutcliffe left the band and McCartney reluctantly became their bass player.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-27"><a href="#cite_note-27"><span>[</span>25<span>]</span></a></sup> They recorded professionally for the first time while in Hamburg, credited as the Beat Brothers, as the backing band for English singer <a href="/wiki/Tony_Sheridan" title="Tony Sheridan">Tony Sheridan</a> on the single "<a href="/wiki/My_Bonnie" title="My Bonnie">My Bonnie</a>".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESpitz2005249.E2.80.93251_28-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESpitz2005249.E2.80.93251-28"><span>[</span>26<span>]</span></a></sup> This brought them to the attention of <a href="/wiki/Brian_Epstein" title="Brian Epstein">Brian Epstein</a>, a key figure in their subsequent development and success. He became their manager in January 1962.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMiles199784.E2.80.9388_29-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMiles199784.E2.80.9388-29"><span>[</span>27<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Ringo_Starr" title="Ringo Starr">Ringo Starr</a> replaced Best in August, and the band had their first hit, "<a href="/wiki/Love_Me_Do" title="Love Me Do">Love Me Do</a>", in October, becoming popular <a href="/wiki/Beatlemania_in_the_United_Kingdom" title="Beatlemania in the United Kingdom">in the UK in 1963</a>, and <a href="/wiki/The_Beatles_in_the_United_States" title="The Beatles in the United States">in the US</a> a year later. Their fans' hysteria became known as "<a href="/wiki/Beatlemania" title="Beatlemania">Beatlemania</a>", and the press sometimes referred to McCartney as the "cute Beatle".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-30"><a href="#cite_note-30"><span>[</span>28<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-32"><a href="#cite_note-32"><span>[</span>nb 3<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-34"><a href="#cite_note-34"><span>[</span>nb 4<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>In August 1965, the Beatles released the McCartney composition "<a href="/wiki/Yesterday_(Beatles_song)" title="Yesterday (Beatles song)">Yesterday</a>", featuring a <a href="/wiki/String_quartet" title="String quartet">string quartet</a>. Included on the <i><a href="/wiki/Help!_(album)" title="Help! (album)">Help!</a></i> LP, the song was the group's first recorded use of classical music elements and their first recording that involved only a single band member.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-35"><a href="#cite_note-35"><span>[</span>31<span>]</span></a></sup> "Yesterday" became the most covered song in popular music history.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-36"><a href="#cite_note-36"><span>[</span>32<span>]</span></a></sup> Later that year, during recording sessions for the album <i><a href="/wiki/Rubber_Soul" title="Rubber Soul">Rubber Soul</a></i>, McCartney began to supplant Lennon as the dominant musical force in the band. <a href="/wiki/Musicology" title="Musicology">Musicologist</a> <a href="/wiki/Ian_MacDonald" title="Ian MacDonald">Ian MacDonald</a> wrote, "from [1965] ... [McCartney] would be in the ascendant not only as a songwriter, but also as instrumentalist, arranger, producer, and <i>de facto</i> musical director".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMacDonald2005172_37-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMacDonald2005172-37"><span>[</span>33<span>]</span></a></sup> Critics described <i>Rubber Soul</i> as a significant advance in the refinement and profundity of the band's music and lyrics.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38"><a href="#cite_note-38"><span>[</span>34<span>]</span></a></sup> Considered a high point in the Beatles catalogue, both Lennon and McCartney claimed to have written the music for the song, "<a href="/wiki/In_My_Life" title="In My Life">In My Life</a>".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-39"><a href="#cite_note-39"><span>[</span>35<span>]</span></a></sup> McCartney said of the album, "we'd had our cute period, and now it was time to expand."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEThe_Beatles2000197_40-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEThe_Beatles2000197-40"><span>[</span>36<span>]</span></a></sup> Recording engineer <a href="/wiki/Norman_Smith_(record_producer)" title="Norman Smith (record producer)">Norman Smith</a> stated that the <i>Rubber Soul</i> sessions exposed indications of increasing contention within the band: "the clash between John and Paul was becoming obvious ... [and] as far as Paul was concerned, George [Harrison] could do no right—Paul was absolutely finicky."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHarry2000b780_41-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHarry2000b780-41"><span>[</span>37<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>In 1966, the Beatles released the album <i><a href="/wiki/Revolver_(Beatles_album)" title="Revolver (Beatles album)">Revolver</a></i>. Featuring sophisticated lyrics, studio experimentation, and an expanded repertoire of <a href="/wiki/Music_genre" title="Music genre">musical genres</a> ranging from innovative string arrangements to <a href="/wiki/Psychedelic_rock" title="Psychedelic rock">psychedelic rock</a>, the album marked an artistic leap for the Beatles.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGould2007348_42-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGould2007348-42"><span>[</span>38<span>]</span></a></sup> The first of three consecutive McCartney <a href="/wiki/A-side_and_B-side" title="A-side and B-side">A-sides</a>, the single "<a href="/wiki/Paperback_Writer" title="Paperback Writer">Paperback Writer</a>" preceded the LP's release.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-43"><a href="#cite_note-43"><span>[</span>39<span>]</span></a></sup> The Beatles produced a short promotional film for the song, and another for its B-side, "<a href="/wiki/Rain_(Beatles_song)" title="Rain (Beatles song)">Rain</a>". The films, described by Harrison as "the forerunner of <a href="/wiki/Music_video" title="Music video">videos</a>", aired on <i><a href="/wiki/The_Ed_Sullivan_Show" title="The Ed Sullivan Show">The Ed Sullivan Show</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Top_of_the_Pops" title="Top of the Pops">Top of the Pops</a></i> in June 1966.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-44"><a href="#cite_note-44"><span>[</span>40<span>]</span></a></sup> <i>Revolver</i> also included McCartney's "<a href="/wiki/Eleanor_Rigby" title="Eleanor Rigby">Eleanor Rigby</a>", which featured a <a href="/wiki/Octet_(music)" title="Octet (music)">string octet</a>. According to Gould, the song is "a neoclassical tour de force ... a true hybrid, conforming to no recognizable style or genre of song".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-45"><a href="#cite_note-45"><span>[</span>41<span>]</span></a></sup> Except for some backing vocals, the song included only McCartney's lead vocal and the strings arranged by producer <a href="/wiki/George_Martin" title="George Martin">George Martin</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHarry2002313.E2.80.93316_46-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHarry2002313.E2.80.93316-46"><span>[</span>42<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-48"><a href="#cite_note-48"><span>[</span>nb 5<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Sgt._Pepper%27s_Lonely_Hearts_Club_Band.jpg"><img alt='An image of the Beatles, holding marching band instruments and wearing colourful uniforms, standing near a grave covered with flowers that spell "Beatles". Standing behind the band are several dozen famous people.' class="thumbimage" data-file-height="300" data-file-width="300" height="220" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/5/50/Sgt._Pepper%27s_Lonely_Hearts_Club_Band.jpg/220px-Sgt._Pepper%27s_Lonely_Hearts_Club_Band.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/5/50/Sgt._Pepper%27s_Lonely_Hearts_Club_Band.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/5/50/Sgt._Pepper%27s_Lonely_Hearts_Club_Band.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Sgt._Pepper%27s_Lonely_Hearts_Club_Band.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<i>Sgt. Pepper's Lonely Hearts Club Band</i>, "the most famous cover of any music album", wrote Beatles biographer <a href="/wiki/Bill_Harry" title="Bill Harry">Bill Harry</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHarry2000a970_49-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHarry2000a970-49"><span>[</span>44<span>]</span></a></sup></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The band gave their final commercial concert at the end of their <a href="/wiki/The_Beatles%27_1966_US_tour" title="The Beatles' 1966 US tour">1966 US tour</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELewisohn1992230_50-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELewisohn1992230-50"><span>[</span>45<span>]</span></a></sup> Later that year, McCartney completed his first musical project apart from the group—a <a href="/wiki/Film_score" title="Film score">film score</a> for the UK production <i><a href="/wiki/The_Family_Way_(soundtrack)" title="The Family Way (soundtrack)">The Family Way</a></i>. The score was a collaboration with Martin, who used two McCartney themes to write thirteen variations. The soundtrack failed to chart, but it won McCartney an <a href="/wiki/Ivor_Novello_Awards" title="Ivor Novello Awards">Ivor Novello Award</a> for Best Instrumental Theme.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBlaney20078_51-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBlaney20078-51"><span>[</span>46<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Upon the end of the Beatles' performing career, McCartney sensed unease in the band and wanted them to maintain creative productivity. He pressed them to start a new project, which became <i><a href="/wiki/Sgt._Pepper%27s_Lonely_Hearts_Club_Band" title="Sgt. Pepper's Lonely Hearts Club Band">Sgt. Pepper's Lonely Hearts Club Band</a></i>, widely regarded as <a href="/wiki/Rock_music" title="Rock music">rock</a>'s first <a href="/wiki/Concept_album" title="Concept album">concept album</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-52"><a href="#cite_note-52"><span>[</span>47<span>]</span></a></sup> Inspired to create a new <a href="/wiki/Persona" title="Persona">persona</a> for the group, to serve as a vehicle for experimentation and to demonstrate to their fans that they had musically matured, McCartney invented the fictional band of the album's <a href="/wiki/Sgt._Pepper%27s_Lonely_Hearts_Club_Band_(song)" title="Sgt. Pepper's Lonely Hearts Club Band (song)">title track</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-53"><a href="#cite_note-53"><span>[</span>48<span>]</span></a></sup> As McCartney explained, "We were fed up with being the Beatles. We really hated that fucking four little <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mop-top" title="Mop-top">mop-top</a> approach. We were not boys we were men ... and [we] thought of ourselves as artists rather than just performers."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMiles1997303_54-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMiles1997303-54"><span>[</span>49<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Starting in November 1966, the band adopted an experimental attitude during recording sessions for the album.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELewisohn1992232_55-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELewisohn1992232-55"><span>[</span>50<span>]</span></a></sup> According to engineer <a href="/wiki/Geoff_Emerick" title="Geoff Emerick">Geoff Emerick</a>, "the Beatles were looking to go out on a limb, both musically and sonically ... we were utilising a lot of <a href="/wiki/Magnetic_tape" title="Magnetic tape">tape</a> <a href="/wiki/Pitch_control" title="Pitch control">varispeeding</a> and other manipulation techniques ... <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Compressor_limiter" title="Compressor limiter">limiters</a> and ... effects like <a href="/wiki/Flanging" title="Flanging">flanging</a> and <a href="/wiki/Automatic_double_tracking" title="Automatic double tracking">ADT</a>."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-56"><a href="#cite_note-56"><span>[</span>51<span>]</span></a></sup> Their recording of "<a href="/wiki/A_Day_in_the_Life" title="A Day in the Life">A Day in the Life</a>" required a forty-piece orchestra, which Martin and McCartney took turns conducting.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-57"><a href="#cite_note-57"><span>[</span>52<span>]</span></a></sup> The sessions produced the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Double_A-side" title="Double A-side">double A-side</a> single "<a href="/wiki/Strawberry_Fields_Forever" title="Strawberry Fields Forever">Strawberry Fields Forever</a>"/"<a href="/wiki/Penny_Lane" title="Penny Lane">Penny Lane</a>" in February 1967, and the LP followed in June.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELewisohn1992350.E2.80.93351_31-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELewisohn1992350.E2.80.93351-31"><span>[</span>29<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-59"><a href="#cite_note-59"><span>[</span>nb 6<span>]</span></a></sup> McCartney's "<a href="/wiki/She%27s_Leaving_Home" title="She's Leaving Home">She's Leaving Home</a>" was an orchestral pop song. MacDonald described the track as "[among] the finest work on <i>Sgt. Pepper</i> — imperishable popular art of its time."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMacDonald2005245_60-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMacDonald2005245-60"><span>[</span>54<span>]</span></a></sup> Based on an ink drawing by McCartney, the LP's cover included a collage designed by <a href="/wiki/Pop_art" title="Pop art">pop artists</a> <a href="/wiki/Peter_Blake_(artist)" title="Peter Blake (artist)">Peter Blake</a> and <a href="/wiki/Jann_Haworth" title="Jann Haworth">Jann Haworth</a>, featuring the Beatles in costume as the Sgt. Pepper's Lonely Hearts Club Band, standing with <a href="/wiki/List_of_images_on_the_cover_of_Sgt._Pepper%27s_Lonely_Hearts_Club_Band" title="List of images on the cover of Sgt. Pepper's Lonely Hearts Club Band">a host of celebrities</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-61"><a href="#cite_note-61"><span>[</span>55<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-63"><a href="#cite_note-63"><span>[</span>nb 7<span>]</span></a></sup> The heavy moustaches worn by the Beatles reflected the growing influence of <a href="/wiki/Hippie" title="Hippie">hippie</a> style trends on the band, while their clothing "spoofed the vogue in Britain for military fashions", wrote Gould.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-64"><a href="#cite_note-64"><span>[</span>57<span>]</span></a></sup> Scholar David Scott Kastan described <i>Sgt. Pepper</i> as "the most important and influential rock-and-roll album ever recorded".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKastan2006139_65-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKastan2006139-65"><span>[</span>58<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<div class="quotebox" style="float: right; clear: right; margin: 0.5em 0 0.8em 1.4em; width:25%; padding: 6px; border: 1px solid #aaa; font-size: 88%; background-color: #F9F9F9; padding:8px;">
<div class="" style="position: relative; text-align: left;">
<div>
<p>"After Brian died ... Paul took over and supposedly led us you know ... we went round in circles ... We broke up then. That was the disintegration. I thought, 'we've fuckin' had it.'"<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWennerGeorge-Warren200024.E2.80.9325_66-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWennerGeorge-Warren200024.E2.80.9325-66"><span>[</span>59<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
</div>
</div>
<div style="text-align: left;">—John Lennon, <i>Rolling Stone</i> magazine, 1970</div>
</div>
<p>Epstein's death in August 1967 created a void, which left the Beatles perplexed and concerned about their future.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBrownGaines2002247_67-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBrownGaines2002247-67"><span>[</span>60<span>]</span></a></sup> McCartney, stepping in to fill that void, gradually became the <i>de facto</i> leader and business manager of the group Lennon had once led.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBenitez20108.E2.80.939_68-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBenitez20108.E2.80.939-68"><span>[</span>61<span>]</span></a></sup> His first creative suggestion after this change of leadership was to propose that the band move forward on their plans to produce a film for television, which was to become <i><a href="/wiki/Magical_Mystery_Tour_(film)" title="Magical Mystery Tour (film)">Magical Mystery Tour</a></i>. The project was "an administrative nightmare throughout", according to Beatles' historian <a href="/wiki/Mark_Lewisohn" title="Mark Lewisohn">Mark Lewisohn</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELewisohn1992238.E2.80.93239_69-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELewisohn1992238.E2.80.93239-69"><span>[</span>62<span>]</span></a></sup> McCartney largely directed the film, which brought the group their first unfavourable critical response.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGould2007455.E2.80.93456_70-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGould2007455.E2.80.93456-70"><span>[</span>63<span>]</span></a></sup> However, the <a href="/wiki/Magical_Mystery_Tour" title="Magical Mystery Tour">film's soundtrack</a> was more successful. It was released in the UK as a six-track double <a href="/wiki/Extended_play" title="Extended play">extended play</a> disc (EP), and as an identically titled LP in the US, filled out with five songs from the band's recent singles.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELewisohn1992350.E2.80.93351_31-2"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELewisohn1992350.E2.80.93351-31"><span>[</span>29<span>]</span></a></sup> The only Capitol compilation later included in the group's official canon of studio albums, the <i>Magical Mystery Tour</i> LP achieved $8 million in sales within three weeks of its release, higher initial sales than any other Capitol LP up to that point.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHarry2000a699_71-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHarry2000a699-71"><span>[</span>64<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>In January 1968, EMI filmed the Beatles for a <a href="/wiki/Trailer_(promotion)" title="Trailer (promotion)">promotional trailer</a> intended to advertise the animated film <i><a href="/wiki/Yellow_Submarine_(film)" title="Yellow Submarine (film)">Yellow Submarine</a></i>, loosely based on the imaginary world evoked by McCartney's 1966 <a href="/wiki/Yellow_Submarine_(song)" title="Yellow Submarine (song)">composition</a>. Though critics admired the film for its visual style, humour and music, the <a href="/wiki/Yellow_Submarine_(album)" title="Yellow Submarine (album)">soundtrack album</a> issued seven months later received a less enthusiastic response.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-72"><a href="#cite_note-72"><span>[</span>65<span>]</span></a></sup> By late 1968, relations within the band were deteriorating. The tension grew while recording <i><a href="/wiki/The_Beatles_(album)" title="The Beatles (album)">the <i>White Album</i></a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELewisohn1992276.E2.80.93304_73-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELewisohn1992276.E2.80.93304-73"><span>[</span>66<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-75"><a href="#cite_note-75"><span>[</span>nb 8<span>]</span></a></sup> Matters worsened the following year during the <i><a href="/wiki/Let_It_Be" title="Let It Be">Let It Be</a></i> sessions, when a camera crew filmed McCartney lecturing the group: "We've been very negative since Mr. Epstein passed away ... we were always fighting [his] discipline a bit, but it's silly to fight that discipline if it's our own".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-76"><a href="#cite_note-76"><span>[</span>68<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>In March 1969, McCartney married <a href="/wiki/Linda_McCartney" title="Linda McCartney">Linda Eastman</a>, and in August, the couple had their first child, <a href="/wiki/Mary_McCartney" title="Mary McCartney">Mary</a>, named after his late mother.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-77"><a href="#cite_note-77"><span>[</span>69<span>]</span></a></sup> For <i><a href="/wiki/Abbey_Road" title="Abbey Road">Abbey Road</a></i>, the band's last recorded album, Martin suggested "a continuously moving piece of music", urging the group to think <a href="/wiki/Symphony" title="Symphony">symphonically</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGould2007563_78-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGould2007563-78"><span>[</span>70<span>]</span></a></sup> McCartney agreed, but Lennon did not. They eventually compromised, agreeing to McCartney's suggestion: an LP featuring individual songs on side one, and a long <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Medley_(music)" title="Medley (music)">medley</a> on side two.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGould2007563_78-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGould2007563-78"><span>[</span>70<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-80"><a href="#cite_note-80"><span>[</span>nb 9<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>On 10 April 1970, in the midst of business disagreements with his bandmates, McCartney announced his departure from the group.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-81"><a href="#cite_note-81"><span>[</span>72<span>]</span></a></sup> He filed suit for the band's formal dissolution on 31 December 1970. More legal disputes followed as McCartney's attorneys, his in-laws <a href="/wiki/Lee_Eastman" title="Lee Eastman">John and Lee Eastman</a>, fought Lennon's, Harrison's, and Starr's business manager, <a href="/wiki/Allen_Klein" title="Allen Klein">Allen Klein</a>, over royalties and creative control. An English court legally dissolved the Beatles on 9 January 1975, though sporadic lawsuits against their record company <a href="/wiki/EMI" title="EMI">EMI</a>, Klein, and each other persisted until 1989.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBenitez20108.E2.80.939_68-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBenitez20108.E2.80.939-68"><span>[</span>61<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-83"><a href="#cite_note-83"><span>[</span>nb 10<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-87"><a href="#cite_note-87"><span>[</span>nb 11<span>]</span></a></sup> They are widely regarded as one of the most popular and influential acts in the history of rock music.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-88"><a href="#cite_note-88"><span>[</span>77<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="1970.E2.80.931981:_Wings">1970–1981: Wings</span></h3>
<div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Paul_McCartney_and_Wings" title="Paul McCartney and Wings">Paul McCartney and Wings</a></div>
<div class="quotebox" style="float: right; clear: right; margin: 0.5em 0 0.8em 1.4em; width:25%; padding: 6px; border: 1px solid #aaa; font-size: 88%; background-color: #F9F9F9; padding:8px;">
<div class="" style="position: relative; text-align: left;">
<div>
<p>"I didn't really want to keep going as a solo artist ... so it became obvious that I had to get a band together ... Linda and I talked it through and it was like, 'Yeah, but let's not put together a supergroup, let's go back to square one.'"<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELewisohn200229_89-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELewisohn200229-89"><span>[</span>78<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
</div>
</div>
<div style="text-align: left;">—McCartney</div>
</div>
<p>After the Beatles' break-up in 1970, McCartney continued his musical career with his first solo release, <i><a href="/wiki/McCartney_(album)" title="McCartney (album)">McCartney</a></i>, a US number-one album. Apart from some vocal contributions from Linda, <i>McCartney</i> is a one-man album, with Paul providing compositions, instrumentation and vocals.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-90"><a href="#cite_note-90"><span>[</span>79<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-92"><a href="#cite_note-92"><span>[</span>nb 12<span>]</span></a></sup> In 1971, he collaborated with Linda and drummer Denny Seiwell on a second album, <i><a href="/wiki/Ram_(album)" title="Ram (album)">Ram</a></i>. A UK number one and a US top five, <i>Ram</i> included the co-written US number-one <a href="/wiki/Hit_single" title="Hit single">hit single</a> "<a href="/wiki/Uncle_Albert/Admiral_Halsey" title="Uncle Albert/Admiral Halsey">Uncle Albert/Admiral Halsey</a>".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-93"><a href="#cite_note-93"><span>[</span>81<span>]</span></a></sup> Later that year, <a href="/wiki/The_Moody_Blues" title="The Moody Blues">ex-Moody Blues</a> guitarist Denny Laine joined the McCartneys and Seiwell to form the band <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Wings_(band)" title="Wings (band)">Wings</a>. McCartney had this to say on the groups's formation: "Wings were always a difficult idea ... any group having to follow [the Beatles'] success would have a hard job ... I found myself in that very position. However, it was a choice between going on or finishing, and I loved music too much to think of stopping."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELewisohn20027_94-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELewisohn20027-94"><span>[</span>82<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-96"><a href="#cite_note-96"><span>[</span>nb 13<span>]</span></a></sup> In September 1971, the McCartneys' daughter <a href="/wiki/Stella_McCartney" title="Stella McCartney">Stella</a> was born, named in honour of Linda's grandmothers, both of whom were named Stella.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-97"><a href="#cite_note-97"><span>[</span>84<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Paul_McCartney_930-6404.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="849" data-file-width="1280" height="146" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2e/Paul_McCartney_930-6404.jpg/220px-Paul_McCartney_930-6404.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2e/Paul_McCartney_930-6404.jpg/330px-Paul_McCartney_930-6404.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2e/Paul_McCartney_930-6404.jpg/440px-Paul_McCartney_930-6404.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Paul_McCartney_930-6404.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Paul McCartney on January 26, 1980</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Following the addition of guitarist <a href="/wiki/Henry_McCullough" title="Henry McCullough">Henry McCullough</a>, Wings' first concert tour began in 1972 with a debut performance in front of an audience of seven hundred at the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Nottingham" title="University of Nottingham">University of Nottingham</a>. Ten more dates followed as they travelled across the UK in a van during an unannounced <a href="/wiki/Wings_University_Tour" title="Wings University Tour">tour of universities</a>, during which the band stayed in modest accommodation and received pay in <a href="/wiki/Coin" title="Coin">coinage</a> collected from students, while avoiding Beatles songs during their performances.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-98"><a href="#cite_note-98"><span>[</span>85<span>]</span></a></sup> A seven-week, <a href="/wiki/Wings_Over_Europe_Tour" title="Wings Over Europe Tour">25-show tour</a> of Europe followed, during which the band played solely Wings and McCartney solo material except for a few covers, including the Little Richard hit "Long Tall Sally", the only song McCartney played during the tour that had previously been recorded by the Beatles. McCartney wanted the tour to avoid large venues; most of the small halls they played had capacities of fewer than 3,000 people.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHarry2002845_99-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHarry2002845-99"><span>[</span>86<span>]</span></a></sup> Of his first two post-Beatles tours, McCartney said, "The main thing I didn't want was to come on stage, faced with the whole torment of five rows of press people with little pads, all looking at me and saying, 'Oh well, he is not as good as he was.' So we decided to go out on that university tour which made me less nervous ... by the end of that tour I felt ready for something else, so we went into Europe."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHarry2002847_100-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHarry2002847-100"><span>[</span>87<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>In March 1973, Wings achieved their first US number-one single, "<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/My_Love_(Paul_McCartney_and_Wings_song)" title="My Love (Paul McCartney and Wings song)">My Love</a>", included on their second LP, <i><a href="/wiki/Red_Rose_Speedway" title="Red Rose Speedway">Red Rose Speedway</a></i>, a US number one and UK top five.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-101"><a href="#cite_note-101"><span>[</span>88<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-102"><a href="#cite_note-102"><span>[</span>nb 14<span>]</span></a></sup> Paul's collaboration with Linda and former Beatles producer Martin resulted in the song "<a href="/wiki/Live_and_Let_Die_(song)" title="Live and Let Die (song)">Live and Let Die</a>", which was the theme song for the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/James_Bond_(film_series)" title="James Bond (film series)">James Bond</a> film <a href="/wiki/Live_and_Let_Die_(film)" title="Live and Let Die (film)">of the same name</a>. Nominated for an <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Academy_Award" title="Academy Award">Academy Award</a>, the song reached number two in the US and number nine in the UK. It also earned Martin a <a href="/wiki/Grammy_Award" title="Grammy Award">Grammy</a> for his orchestral arrangement.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-103"><a href="#cite_note-103"><span>[</span>89<span>]</span></a></sup> Music professor and author Vincent Benitez described the track as "<a href="/wiki/Symphonic_rock" title="Symphonic rock">symphonic rock</a> at its best".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-104"><a href="#cite_note-104"><span>[</span>90<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-106"><a href="#cite_note-106"><span>[</span>nb 15<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>After the departure of McCullough and Seiwell in 1973, the McCartneys and Laine recorded <i><a href="/wiki/Band_on_the_Run" title="Band on the Run">Band on the Run</a></i>. The album was the first of seven platinum Wings LPs.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMcGee2003248.E2.80.93249_107-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMcGee2003248.E2.80.93249-107"><span>[</span>92<span>]</span></a></sup> It was a US and UK number one, the band's first to top the charts in both countries and the first ever to reach <i>Billboard</i> magazine's charts on three separate occasions. One of the best-selling releases of the decade, it remained on the UK charts for 124 weeks. <i><a href="/wiki/Rolling_Stone" title="Rolling Stone">Rolling Stone</a></i> named it Album of the Year for 1974, and in 1975 it won Grammy Awards for Best Contemporary/Pop Vocal and Best Engineered Album.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-108"><a href="#cite_note-108"><span>[</span>93<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-110"><a href="#cite_note-110"><span>[</span>nb 16<span>]</span></a></sup> In 1974, Wings achieved a second US number-one single with <a href="/wiki/Band_on_the_Run_(song)" title="Band on the Run (song)">the title track</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-111"><a href="#cite_note-111"><span>[</span>95<span>]</span></a></sup> The album also included the top-ten hits "<a href="/wiki/Jet_(song)" title="Jet (song)">Jet</a>" and "<a href="/wiki/Helen_Wheels" title="Helen Wheels">Helen Wheels</a>", and earned the 413th spot on <i>Rolling Stone's</i> list of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/The_500_Greatest_Albums_of_All_Time" title="The 500 Greatest Albums of All Time">the 500 Greatest Albums of All Time</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-112"><a href="#cite_note-112"><span>[</span>96<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-114"><a href="#cite_note-114"><span>[</span>nb 17<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Paul_McCartney_during_a_Wings_concert,_1976.jpg"><img alt="Coloured image of a long-haired McCartney in the 1970s playing a guitar." class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1952" data-file-width="1713" height="194" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/09/Paul_McCartney_during_a_Wings_concert%2C_1976.jpg/170px-Paul_McCartney_during_a_Wings_concert%2C_1976.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/09/Paul_McCartney_during_a_Wings_concert%2C_1976.jpg/255px-Paul_McCartney_during_a_Wings_concert%2C_1976.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/09/Paul_McCartney_during_a_Wings_concert%2C_1976.jpg/340px-Paul_McCartney_during_a_Wings_concert%2C_1976.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Paul_McCartney_during_a_Wings_concert,_1976.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
McCartney during a Wings concert, 1976</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Wings followed <i>Band on the Run</i> with the chart-topping albums <i><a href="/wiki/Venus_and_Mars_(Wings_album)" title="Venus and Mars (Wings album)">Venus and Mars</a></i> (1975) and <i><a href="/wiki/Wings_at_the_Speed_of_Sound" title="Wings at the Speed of Sound">Wings at the Speed of Sound</a></i> (1976).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-115"><a href="#cite_note-115"><span>[</span>98<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-117"><a href="#cite_note-117"><span>[</span>nb 18<span>]</span></a></sup> In 1975, they began the fourteen-month <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Wings_Over_the_World_Tour" title="Wings Over the World Tour">Wings Over the World Tour</a>, which included stops in the UK, Australia, Europe and the US. The tour marked the first time McCartney performed Beatles songs live with Wings, with five in the two-hour <a href="/wiki/Set_list" title="Set list">set list</a>: "I've Just Seen a Face", "Yesterday", "Blackbird", "Lady Madonna" and "The Long and Winding Road".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-118"><a href="#cite_note-118"><span>[</span>100<span>]</span></a></sup> Following the second European leg of the tour and extensive rehearsals in London, the group undertook an ambitious US <a href="/wiki/Arena" title="Arena">arena</a> tour that yielded the US number-one <a href="/wiki/Live_album" title="Live album">live</a> triple LP <i><a href="/wiki/Wings_over_America" title="Wings over America">Wings over America</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-119"><a href="#cite_note-119"><span>[</span>101<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>In September 1977, the McCartneys had a third child, a son they named <a href="/wiki/James_McCartney" title="James McCartney">James</a>. In November, the Wings song "<a href="/wiki/Mull_of_Kintyre_(song)" title="Mull of Kintyre (song)">Mull of Kintyre</a>", co-written with Laine, was quickly becoming one of the best-selling singles in UK chart history.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-120"><a href="#cite_note-120"><span>[</span>102<span>]</span></a></sup> The most successful single of McCartney's solo career, it achieved double the sales of the previous record holder, "<a href="/wiki/She_Loves_You" title="She Loves You">She Loves You</a>", and went on to sell 2.5 million copies and hold the UK sales record until the 1984 charity single, "<a href="/wiki/Do_They_Know_It%27s_Christmas%3F" title="Do They Know It's Christmas?">Do They Know It's Christmas?</a>".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-121"><a href="#cite_note-121"><span>[</span>103<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-123"><a href="#cite_note-123"><span>[</span>nb 19<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p><i><a href="/wiki/London_Town_(Wings_album)" title="London Town (Wings album)">London Town</a></i> (1978) spawned a US number-one single ("<a href="/wiki/With_a_Little_Luck" title="With a Little Luck">With a Little Luck</a>"), and was Wings' best-selling LP since <i>Band on the Run</i>, making the top five in both the US and the UK. Critical reception was unfavourable, and McCartney expressed disappointment with the album.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBlaney2007122.E2.80.93125_124-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBlaney2007122.E2.80.93125-124"><span>[</span>105<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-126"><a href="#cite_note-126"><span>[</span>nb 20<span>]</span></a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/Back_to_the_Egg" title="Back to the Egg">Back to the Egg</a></i> (1979) featured McCartney's collaboration with a rock <a href="/wiki/Supergroup_(music)" title="Supergroup (music)">supergroup</a> dubbed <a href="/wiki/Rockestra_Theme" title="Rockestra Theme">"the Rockestra"</a>. Credited to Wings, the band included <a href="/wiki/Pete_Townshend" title="Pete Townshend">Pete Townshend</a>, <a href="/wiki/David_Gilmour" title="David Gilmour">David Gilmour</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gary_Brooker" title="Gary Brooker">Gary Brooker</a>, <a href="/wiki/John_Paul_Jones_(musician)" title="John Paul Jones (musician)">John Paul Jones</a> and <a href="/wiki/John_Bonham" title="John Bonham">John Bonham</a>. Though certified platinum, critics panned <i>Back to the Egg</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-127"><a href="#cite_note-127"><span>[</span>107<span>]</span></a></sup> Wings completed their final concert tour in 1979, with <a href="/wiki/Wings_UK_Tour_1979" title="Wings UK Tour 1979">twenty shows in the UK</a> that included the live debut of the Beatles songs "<a href="/wiki/Got_to_Get_You_into_My_Life" title="Got to Get You into My Life">Got to Get You into My Life</a>", "<a href="/wiki/The_Fool_on_the_Hill" title="The Fool on the Hill">The Fool on the Hill</a>" and "Let it Be".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-128"><a href="#cite_note-128"><span>[</span>108<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>In 1980, McCartney released his second solo LP, the self-produced <i><a href="/wiki/McCartney_II" title="McCartney II">McCartney II</a></i>, which peaked at number one in the UK and number three in the US. As with his first album, he composed and performed it alone.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-129"><a href="#cite_note-129"><span>[</span>109<span>]</span></a></sup> The album contained the song "<a href="/wiki/Coming_Up_(song)" title="Coming Up (song)">Coming Up</a>", the live version of which, recorded in <a href="/wiki/Glasgow" title="Glasgow">Glasgow</a>, Scotland, in 1979 by Wings, became the group's last number-one hit.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-130"><a href="#cite_note-130"><span>[</span>110<span>]</span></a></sup> By 1981, McCartney felt he had accomplished all he could creatively with Wings and decided he needed a change. The group disbanded in April 1981 following disagreements over royalties and salaries.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBenitez201096.E2.80.9397_131-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBenitez201096.E2.80.9397-131"><span>[</span>111<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-133"><a href="#cite_note-133"><span>[</span>nb 21<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-136"><a href="#cite_note-136"><span>[</span>nb 22<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="1982.E2.80.931990">1982–1990</span></h3>
<p>In 1982 McCartney collaborated with <a href="/wiki/Stevie_Wonder" title="Stevie Wonder">Stevie Wonder</a> on the Martin-produced number-one hit "<a href="/wiki/Ebony_and_Ivory" title="Ebony and Ivory">Ebony and Ivory</a>", included on McCartney's <i><a href="/wiki/Tug_of_War_(Paul_McCartney_album)" title="Tug of War (Paul McCartney album)">Tug of War</a></i> LP, and with <a href="/wiki/Michael_Jackson" title="Michael Jackson">Michael Jackson</a> on "<a href="/wiki/The_Girl_Is_Mine" title="The Girl Is Mine">The Girl Is Mine</a>" from <i><a href="/wiki/Thriller_(Michael_Jackson_album)" title="Thriller (Michael Jackson album)">Thriller</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-137"><a href="#cite_note-137"><span>[</span>115<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-139"><a href="#cite_note-139"><span>[</span>nb 23<span>]</span></a></sup> "Ebony and Ivory" was McCartney's record 28th single to hit number one on the Billboard 100.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-140"><a href="#cite_note-140"><span>[</span>117<span>]</span></a></sup> The following year, he and Jackson worked on "<a href="/wiki/Say_Say_Say" title="Say Say Say">Say Say Say</a>", McCartney's most recent US number one as of 2014<sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Paul_McCartney&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>. McCartney earned his latest UK number one as of 2014<sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Paul_McCartney&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup> with the title track of his <a href="/wiki/Pipes_of_Peace" title="Pipes of Peace">LP release</a> that year, "<a href="/wiki/Pipes_of_Peace_(song)" title="Pipes of Peace (song)">Pipes of Peace</a>".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-141"><a href="#cite_note-141"><span>[</span>118<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-143"><a href="#cite_note-143"><span>[</span>nb 24<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>In 1984, McCartney starred in the musical <i><a href="/wiki/Give_My_Regards_to_Broad_Street_(film)" title="Give My Regards to Broad Street (film)">Give My Regards to Broad Street</a></i>, a feature film he also wrote and produced which included Starr in an acting role. Disparaged by critics, <i><a href="/wiki/Variety_(magazine)" title="Variety (magazine)">Variety</a></i> described the film as "characterless, bloodless, and pointless".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-144"><a href="#cite_note-144"><span>[</span>120<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Roger_Ebert" title="Roger Ebert">Roger Ebert</a> awarded it a single star and wrote, "you can safely skip the movie and proceed directly to the <a href="/wiki/Give_My_Regards_to_Broad_Street" title="Give My Regards to Broad Street">soundtrack</a>".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-145"><a href="#cite_note-145"><span>[</span>121<span>]</span></a></sup> The album fared much better, reaching number one in the UK and producing the US top-ten hit single "<a href="/wiki/No_More_Lonely_Nights" title="No More Lonely Nights">No More Lonely Nights</a>", featuring David Gilmour on lead guitar.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-146"><a href="#cite_note-146"><span>[</span>122<span>]</span></a></sup> In 1985, <a href="/wiki/Warner_Bros." title="Warner Bros.">Warner Brothers</a> commissioned McCartney to write a song for the comedic feature film <i><a href="/wiki/Spies_Like_Us" title="Spies Like Us">Spies Like Us</a></i>. He composed and recorded <a href="/wiki/Spies_Like_Us_(song)" title="Spies Like Us (song)">the track</a> in four days, with <a href="/wiki/Phil_Ramone" title="Phil Ramone">Phil Ramone</a> co-producing.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBlaney2007171_147-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBlaney2007171-147"><span>[</span>123<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-149"><a href="#cite_note-149"><span>[</span>nb 25<span>]</span></a></sup> McCartney participated in <a href="/wiki/Live_Aid" title="Live Aid">Live Aid</a>, performing "Let it Be", but technical difficulties rendered his vocals and piano barely audible for the first two verses, punctuated by squeals of <a href="/wiki/Audio_feedback" title="Audio feedback">feedback</a>. Equipment technicians resolved the problems and <a href="/wiki/David_Bowie" title="David Bowie">David Bowie</a>, <a href="/wiki/Alison_Moyet" title="Alison Moyet">Alison Moyet</a>, Pete Townshend and <a href="/wiki/Bob_Geldof" title="Bob Geldof">Bob Geldof</a> joined McCartney on stage, receiving an enthusiastic crowd reaction.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESounes2010402.E2.80.93403_150-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESounes2010402.E2.80.93403-150"><span>[</span>125<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>McCartney collaborated with <a href="/wiki/Eric_Stewart" title="Eric Stewart">Eric Stewart</a> on <i><a href="/wiki/Press_to_Play" title="Press to Play">Press to Play</a></i> (1986), with Stewart co-writing more than half the songs on the LP.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBlaney2007177_151-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBlaney2007177-151"><span>[</span>126<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-153"><a href="#cite_note-153"><span>[</span>nb 26<span>]</span></a></sup> In 1988, McCartney released <i><a href="/wiki/Choba_B_CCCP" title="Choba B CCCP">Choba B CCCP</a></i>, released only in the <a href="/wiki/Soviet_Union" title="Soviet Union">Soviet Union</a>, which contained eighteen <a href="/wiki/Cover_version" title="Cover version">covers</a>; recorded over the course of two days.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-154"><a href="#cite_note-154"><span>[</span>128<span>]</span></a></sup> In 1989, he joined forces with fellow <a href="/wiki/Merseyside" title="Merseyside">Merseysiders</a> <a href="/wiki/Gerry_Marsden" title="Gerry Marsden">Gerry Marsden</a> and <a href="/wiki/Holly_Johnson" title="Holly Johnson">Holly Johnson</a> to record an updated version of "<a href="/wiki/Ferry_Cross_the_Mersey#Charity_record_for_The_Hillsborough_Disaster_Fund" title="Ferry Cross the Mersey">Ferry Cross the Mersey</a>", for the <a href="/wiki/Hillsborough_disaster" title="Hillsborough disaster">Hillsborough disaster</a> appeal fund.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHarry2002327.E2.80.93328_155-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHarry2002327.E2.80.93328-155"><span>[</span>129<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-157"><a href="#cite_note-157"><span>[</span>nb 27<span>]</span></a></sup> That same year, he released <i><a href="/wiki/Flowers_in_the_Dirt" title="Flowers in the Dirt">Flowers in the Dirt</a></i>; a collaborative effort with <a href="/wiki/Elvis_Costello" title="Elvis Costello">Elvis Costello</a> that included musical contributions from Gilmour and <a href="/wiki/Nicky_Hopkins" title="Nicky Hopkins">Nicky Hopkins</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-158"><a href="#cite_note-158"><span>[</span>131<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-160"><a href="#cite_note-160"><span>[</span>nb 28<span>]</span></a></sup> McCartney then formed a band consisting of himself and Linda, with <a href="/wiki/Hamish_Stuart" title="Hamish Stuart">Hamish Stuart</a> and <a href="/wiki/Robbie_McIntosh" title="Robbie McIntosh">Robbie McIntosh</a> on guitars, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Paul_%22Wix%22_Wickens" title='Paul "Wix" Wickens'>Paul "Wix" Wickens</a> on keyboards and <a href="/wiki/Chris_Whitten" title="Chris Whitten">Chris Whitten</a> on drums.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-161"><a href="#cite_note-161"><span>[</span>133<span>]</span></a></sup> In September 1989, they launched <a href="/wiki/The_Paul_McCartney_World_Tour" title="The Paul McCartney World Tour">the Paul McCartney World Tour</a>, his first in over a decade. The following year, he released the triple album, <i><a href="/wiki/Tripping_the_Live_Fantastic" title="Tripping the Live Fantastic">Tripping the Live Fantastic</a></i>, which contained select performances from the tour.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHarry2002851_162-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHarry2002851-162"><span>[</span>134<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-164"><a href="#cite_note-164"><span>[</span>nb 29<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-166"><a href="#cite_note-166"><span>[</span>nb 30<span>]</span></a></sup> In 1990, the US publication <i>Amusement Business</i> presented McCartney with an award for the highest grossing show of the year; his two performances at <a href="/wiki/University_of_California,_Berkeley" title="University of California, Berkeley">Berkeley</a> earned over $3.5 million.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-167"><a href="#cite_note-167"><span>[</span>137<span>]</span></a></sup> He performed for the largest paying stadium audience in history on 21 April 1990, when 184,000 people attended his concert at <a href="/wiki/Maracan%C3%A3_Stadium" title="Maracanã Stadium">Maracanã Stadium</a> in Rio de Janeiro, Brazil.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBadman1999444_168-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBadman1999444-168"><span>[</span>138<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="1991.E2.80.932000">1991–2000</span></h3>
<p>McCartney ventured into <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Orchestral_music" title="Orchestral music">orchestral music</a> in 1991, when the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Royal_Liverpool_Philharmonic_Society" title="Royal Liverpool Philharmonic Society">Royal Liverpool Philharmonic Society</a> commissioned a musical piece by him to celebrate its <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sesquicentennial" title="Sesquicentennial">sesquicentennial</a>. He collaborated with composer <a href="/wiki/Carl_Davis" title="Carl Davis">Carl Davis</a>, producing <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Liverpool_Oratorio" title="Liverpool Oratorio">Liverpool Oratorio</a></i>. The performance featured opera singers <a href="/wiki/Kiri_Te_Kanawa" title="Kiri Te Kanawa">Kiri Te Kanawa</a>, Sally Burgess, <a href="/wiki/Jerry_Hadley" title="Jerry Hadley">Jerry Hadley</a> and <a href="/wiki/Willard_White" title="Willard White">Willard White</a>, with the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Royal_Liverpool_Philharmonic_Orchestra" title="Royal Liverpool Philharmonic Orchestra">Royal Liverpool Philharmonic Orchestra</a> and the choir of <a href="/wiki/Liverpool_Cathedral" title="Liverpool Cathedral">Liverpool Cathedral</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-169"><a href="#cite_note-169"><span>[</span>139<span>]</span></a></sup> Reviews were negative. <i><a href="/wiki/The_Guardian" title="The Guardian">The Guardian</a></i> was especially critical, describing the music as "afraid of anything approaching a fast tempo", and adding that the piece has "little awareness of the need for recurrent ideas that will bind the work into a whole".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHarry2002528_170-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHarry2002528-170"><span>[</span>140<span>]</span></a></sup> The paper published a letter McCartney submitted in response in which he noted several of the work's faster tempos and added, "happily, history shows that many good pieces of music were not liked by the critics of the time so I am content to ... let people judge for themselves the merits of the work."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHarry2002528_170-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHarry2002528-170"><span>[</span>140<span>]</span></a></sup> <i>The New York Times</i> was slightly more generous, stating, "There are moments of beauty and pleasure in this dramatic miscellany ... the music's innocent sincerity makes it difficult to be put off by its ambitions".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-171"><a href="#cite_note-171"><span>[</span>141<span>]</span></a></sup> Performed around the world after its London premiere, the <i>Liverpool Oratorio</i> reached number one on the UK classical chart, <i>Music Week</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-172"><a href="#cite_note-172"><span>[</span>142<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>In 1991, McCartney performed a selection of <a href="/wiki/Acoustic_music" title="Acoustic music">acoustic-only</a> songs on <i><a href="/wiki/MTV_Unplugged" title="MTV Unplugged">MTV Unplugged</a></i> and released a live album of the performance titled <i><a href="/wiki/Unplugged_(The_Official_Bootleg)" title="Unplugged (The Official Bootleg)">Unplugged (The Official Bootleg)</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-173"><a href="#cite_note-173"><span>[</span>143<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-175"><a href="#cite_note-175"><span>[</span>nb 31<span>]</span></a></sup> During the 1990s, McCartney collaborated twice with <a href="/wiki/Martin_Glover" title="Martin Glover">Youth</a> of <a href="/wiki/Killing_Joke" title="Killing Joke">Killing Joke</a> as the musical duo <a href="/wiki/The_Fireman_(band)" title="The Fireman (band)">"the Fireman"</a>. The two released their first <a href="/wiki/Electronica" title="Electronica">electronica</a> album together, <i><a href="/wiki/Strawberries_Oceans_Ships_Forest" title="Strawberries Oceans Ships Forest">Strawberries Oceans Ships Forest</a></i>, in 1993.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHarry2002332.E2.80.93334_176-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHarry2002332.E2.80.93334-176"><span>[</span>145<span>]</span></a></sup> McCartney released the rock album, <i><a href="/wiki/Off_the_Ground" title="Off the Ground">Off the Ground</a></i>, in 1993.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHarry2002656_177-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHarry2002656-177"><span>[</span>146<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-179"><a href="#cite_note-179"><span>[</span>nb 32<span>]</span></a></sup> The subsequent <a href="/wiki/The_New_World_Tour" title="The New World Tour">New World Tour</a> followed, which led to the release of the <i><a href="/wiki/Paul_Is_Live" title="Paul Is Live">Paul Is Live</a></i> album later that year.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-180"><a href="#cite_note-180"><span>[</span>148<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-182"><a href="#cite_note-182"><span>[</span>nb 33<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-185"><a href="#cite_note-185"><span>[</span>nb 34<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Starting in 1994, McCartney took a four-year break from his solo career to work on Apple's <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Beatles_Anthology" title="Beatles Anthology">Beatles Anthology</a></i> project with Harrison, Starr and Martin. He recorded a radio series called <i><a href="/wiki/Oobu_Joobu" title="Oobu Joobu">Oobu Joobu</a></i> in 1995 for the American network <a href="/wiki/Westwood_One_(1976%E2%80%932011)" title="Westwood One (1976–2011)">Westwood One</a>, which he described as "widescreen radio".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMiles1997218.E2.80.93219_186-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMiles1997218.E2.80.93219-186"><span>[</span>152<span>]</span></a></sup> Also in 1995, <a href="/wiki/Charles,_Prince_of_Wales" title="Charles, Prince of Wales">Prince Charles</a> presented him with an Honorary <a href="/wiki/Fellow" title="Fellow">Fellowship</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Royal_College_of_Music" title="Royal College of Music">Royal College of Music</a>—"kind of amazing for somebody who doesn't read a note of music", commented McCartney.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-187"><a href="#cite_note-187"><span>[</span>153<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>In 1997, McCartney released the rock album <i><a href="/wiki/Flaming_Pie" title="Flaming Pie">Flaming Pie</a></i>. Starr appeared on drums and backing vocals in "<a href="/wiki/Beautiful_Night_(Paul_McCartney_song)" title="Beautiful Night (Paul McCartney song)">Beautiful Night</a>".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBlaney2007224_188-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBlaney2007224-188"><span>[</span>154<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-190"><a href="#cite_note-190"><span>[</span>nb 35<span>]</span></a></sup> Later that year, he released the classical work <i><a href="/wiki/Standing_Stone_(album)" title="Standing Stone (album)">Standing Stone</a></i>, which topped the UK and US classical charts.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBlaney2007229_191-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBlaney2007229-191"><span>[</span>156<span>]</span></a></sup> In 1998, he released <i><a href="/wiki/Rushes_(album)" title="Rushes (album)">Rushes</a></i>, the second electronica album by the Fireman.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-192"><a href="#cite_note-192"><span>[</span>157<span>]</span></a></sup> In 1999, McCartney released <i><a href="/wiki/Run_Devil_Run_(album)" title="Run Devil Run (album)">Run Devil Run</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBlaney2007241_193-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBlaney2007241-193"><span>[</span>158<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-194"><a href="#cite_note-194"><span>[</span>nb 36<span>]</span></a></sup> Recorded in one week, and featuring <a href="/wiki/Ian_Paice" title="Ian Paice">Ian Paice</a> and David Gilmour, it was primarily an album of covers with three McCartney originals. He had been planning such an album for years, having been previously encouraged to do so by Linda, who had died of cancer in April 1998.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-195"><a href="#cite_note-195"><span>[</span>159<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>In 1999, he continued his experimentation with orchestral music on <i><a href="/wiki/Working_Classical" title="Working Classical">Working Classical</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHarry2002710.E2.80.93711_196-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHarry2002710.E2.80.93711-196"><span>[</span>160<span>]</span></a></sup> In 2000, he released the electronica album <i><a href="/wiki/Liverpool_Sound_Collage" title="Liverpool Sound Collage">Liverpool Sound Collage</a></i> with <a href="/wiki/Super_Furry_Animals" title="Super Furry Animals">Super Furry Animals</a> and Youth, using the sound collage and <a href="/wiki/Musique_concr%C3%A8te" title="Musique concrète">musique concrète</a> techniques that had fascinated him in the mid-1960s.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHarry2002528.E2.80.93529_197-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHarry2002528.E2.80.93529-197"><span>[</span>161<span>]</span></a></sup> He contributed the song "Nova" to a tribute album of classical, <a href="/wiki/Choir" title="Choir">choral music</a> called <i><a href="/wiki/A_Garland_for_Linda" title="A Garland for Linda">A Garland for Linda</a></i> (2000), dedicated to his late wife.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-198"><a href="#cite_note-198"><span>[</span>162<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="2000.E2.80.932010">2000–2010</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Paul_McCartney_live_in_Dublin2.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1600" data-file-width="1600" height="220" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0e/Paul_McCartney_live_in_Dublin2.jpg/220px-Paul_McCartney_live_in_Dublin2.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0e/Paul_McCartney_live_in_Dublin2.jpg/330px-Paul_McCartney_live_in_Dublin2.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0e/Paul_McCartney_live_in_Dublin2.jpg/440px-Paul_McCartney_live_in_Dublin2.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Paul_McCartney_live_in_Dublin2.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Paul McCartney live in Dublin 2010</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Having witnessed the <a href="/wiki/September_11_attacks" title="September 11 attacks">11 September 2001 attacks</a> from the <a href="/wiki/John_F._Kennedy_International_Airport" title="John F. Kennedy International Airport">JFK airport</a> tarmac, McCartney was inspired to take a leading role in organizing <a href="/wiki/The_Concert_for_New_York_City" title="The Concert for New York City">the Concert for New York City</a>. His studio album release in November that year, <i><a href="/wiki/Driving_Rain" title="Driving Rain">Driving Rain</a></i>, included the song "<a href="/wiki/Freedom_(Paul_McCartney_song)" title="Freedom (Paul McCartney song)">Freedom</a>", written in response to the attacks.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-199"><a href="#cite_note-199"><span>[</span>163<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-201"><a href="#cite_note-201"><span>[</span>nb 37<span>]</span></a></sup> The following year, McCartney went out on tour with a band that included guitarists <a href="/wiki/Rusty_Anderson" title="Rusty Anderson">Rusty Anderson</a> and <a href="/wiki/Brian_Ray" title="Brian Ray">Brian Ray</a>, accompanied by Paul "Wix" Wickens on keyboards and <a href="/wiki/Abe_Laboriel,_Jr." title="Abe Laboriel, Jr.">Abe Laboriel, Jr.</a> on drums.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-202"><a href="#cite_note-202"><span>[</span>165<span>]</span></a></sup> They began the <a href="/wiki/Driving_World_Tour" title="Driving World Tour">Driving World Tour</a> in April 2002, which included stops in the US, Mexico and Japan. The tour resulted in the <a href="/wiki/Double_album" title="Double album">double</a> live album <i><a href="/wiki/Back_in_the_U.S." title="Back in the U.S.">Back in the U.S.</a></i>, released internationally in 2003 as <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Back_in_the_World" title="Back in the World">Back in the World</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESounes2010517.E2.80.93518_203-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESounes2010517.E2.80.93518-203"><span>[</span>166<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-205"><a href="#cite_note-205"><span>[</span>nb 38<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-206"><a href="#cite_note-206"><span>[</span>nb 39<span>]</span></a></sup> The tour earned a reported $126.2 million, an average of over $2 million per night, and Billboard named it the top tour of the year.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-207"><a href="#cite_note-207"><span>[</span>168<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>In July 2002, McCartney married <a href="/wiki/Heather_Mills" title="Heather Mills">Heather Mills</a>. In November, on the first anniversary of George Harrison's death, McCartney performed at the <a href="/wiki/Concert_for_George" title="Concert for George">Concert for George</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-208"><a href="#cite_note-208"><span>[</span>169<span>]</span></a></sup> He participated in the <a href="/wiki/National_Football_League" title="National Football League">National Football League</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Super_Bowl" title="Super Bowl">Super Bowl</a>, performing "Freedom" during the pre-game show for <a href="/wiki/Super_Bowl_XXXVI" title="Super Bowl XXXVI">Super Bowl XXXVI</a> in 2002 and headlining the halftime show at <a href="/wiki/Super_Bowl_XXXIX" title="Super Bowl XXXIX">Super Bowl XXXIX</a> in 2005.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-209"><a href="#cite_note-209"><span>[</span>170<span>]</span></a></sup> The English <a href="/wiki/College_of_Arms" title="College of Arms">College of Arms</a> honoured McCartney in 2002 by granting him a <a href="/wiki/Coat_of_arms" title="Coat of arms">coat of arms</a>. His crest, featuring a <a href="/wiki/Liver_bird" title="Liver bird">Liver bird</a> holding an acoustic guitar in its claw, reflects his background in Liverpool and his musical career. The shield includes four curved emblems which resemble <a href="/wiki/Beetle" title="Beetle">beetles</a>' backs. The arms' motto is <i>Ecce Cor Meum</i>, Latin for "Behold My Heart".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BBCCREST_210-0"><a href="#cite_note-BBCCREST-210"><span>[</span>171<span>]</span></a></sup> In 2003, the McCartneys had a child, Beatrice Milly.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESounes2010523_211-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESounes2010523-211"><span>[</span>172<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Ringo_Starr_e_Paul_Mcartney_-_E3_2009.jpg"><img alt="McCartney and Starr standing on a stage facing each other both with microphones help up to their mouths.
