Both men are wearing dark suits, McCartney is wearing a pink shirt, and Starr a black-and-white print." class="thumbimage" data-file-height="304" data-file-width="528" height="127" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f0/Ringo_Starr_e_Paul_Mcartney_-_E3_2009.jpg/220px-Ringo_Starr_e_Paul_Mcartney_-_E3_2009.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f0/Ringo_Starr_e_Paul_Mcartney_-_E3_2009.jpg/330px-Ringo_Starr_e_Paul_Mcartney_-_E3_2009.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f0/Ringo_Starr_e_Paul_Mcartney_-_E3_2009.jpg/440px-Ringo_Starr_e_Paul_Mcartney_-_E3_2009.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Ringo_Starr_e_Paul_Mcartney_-_E3_2009.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Starr and McCartney promoting <i>The Beatles: Rock Band</i> in 2009</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In July 2005, he performed at the <a href="/wiki/Live_8" title="Live 8">Live 8</a> event in <a href="/wiki/Hyde_Park,_London" title="Hyde Park, London">Hyde Park, London</a>, opening the show with "<a href="/wiki/Sgt._Pepper%27s_Lonely_Hearts_Club_Band_(song)" title="Sgt. Pepper's Lonely Hearts Club Band (song)">Sgt. Pepper's Lonely Hearts Club Band</a>" (with <a href="/wiki/U2" title="U2">U2</a>) and closing it with "<a href="/wiki/Drive_My_Car" title="Drive My Car">Drive My Car</a>" (with <a href="/wiki/George_Michael" title="George Michael">George Michael</a>), "<a href="/wiki/Helter_Skelter_(song)" title="Helter Skelter (song)">Helter Skelter</a>", and "<a href="/wiki/The_Long_and_Winding_Road" title="The Long and Winding Road">The Long and Winding Road</a>".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBlaney2007268.E2.80.93269_212-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBlaney2007268.E2.80.93269-212"><span>[</span>173<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-214"><a href="#cite_note-214"><span>[</span>nb 40<span>]</span></a></sup> In September, he released the rock album <i><a href="/wiki/Chaos_and_Creation_in_the_Backyard" title="Chaos and Creation in the Backyard">Chaos and Creation in the Backyard</a></i>, for which he provided most of the instrumentation.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMolenda200568.E2.80.9370_215-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMolenda200568.E2.80.9370-215"><span>[</span>175<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-217"><a href="#cite_note-217"><span>[</span>nb 41<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-219"><a href="#cite_note-219"><span>[</span>nb 42<span>]</span></a></sup> In 2006, McCartney released the classical work <i><a href="/wiki/Ecce_Cor_Meum" title="Ecce Cor Meum">Ecce Cor Meum</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBlaney2007276_220-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBlaney2007276-220"><span>[</span>178<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-221"><a href="#cite_note-221"><span>[</span>nb 43<span>]</span></a></sup> The rock album <i><a href="/wiki/Memory_Almost_Full" title="Memory Almost Full">Memory Almost Full</a></i> followed in 2007.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESounes2010540.E2.80.93541_222-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESounes2010540.E2.80.93541-222"><span>[</span>179<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-224"><a href="#cite_note-224"><span>[</span>nb 44<span>]</span></a></sup> In 2008, he released his third Fireman album, <i><a href="/wiki/Electric_Arguments" title="Electric Arguments">Electric Arguments</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESounes2010559_225-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESounes2010559-225"><span>[</span>181<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-227"><a href="#cite_note-227"><span>[</span>nb 45<span>]</span></a></sup> Also in 2008, he performed at a concert in Liverpool to celebrate the city's year as <a href="/wiki/European_Capital_of_Culture" title="European Capital of Culture">European Capital of Culture</a>. In 2009, after a four-year break, he returned to touring and has since performed over 80 shows.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-228"><a href="#cite_note-228"><span>[</span>183<span>]</span></a></sup> More than forty-five years after the Beatles first appeared on American television during <i>The Ed Sullivan Show</i>, he returned to the same New York theatre to perform on <i><a href="/wiki/Late_Show_with_David_Letterman" title="Late Show with David Letterman">Late Show with David Letterman</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-229"><a href="#cite_note-229"><span>[</span>184<span>]</span></a></sup> On 9 September 2009, EMI reissued the Beatles catalogue following a four-year digital remastering effort, releasing a music video game called <i><a href="/wiki/The_Beatles:_Rock_Band" title="The Beatles: Rock Band">The Beatles: Rock Band</a></i> the same day.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-230"><a href="#cite_note-230"><span>[</span>185<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>McCartney's enduring fame has made him a popular choice to open new venues. In 2009, he played three sold-out concerts at the newly built <a href="/wiki/Citi_Field" title="Citi Field">Citi Field</a>—a venue constructed to replace <a href="/wiki/Shea_Stadium" title="Shea Stadium">Shea Stadium</a> in <a href="/wiki/Queens" title="Queens">Queens</a>, New York. These performances yielded the double live album <i><a href="/wiki/Good_Evening_New_York_City" title="Good Evening New York City">Good Evening New York City</a></i> later that year.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESounes2010560_231-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESounes2010560-231"><span>[</span>186<span>]</span></a></sup> In 2010, McCartney opened the <a href="/wiki/Consol_Energy_Center" title="Consol Energy Center">Consol Energy Center</a> in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pittsburgh,_Pennsylvania" title="Pittsburgh, Pennsylvania">Pittsburgh, Pennsylvania</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-232"><a href="#cite_note-232"><span>[</span>187<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-234"><a href="#cite_note-234"><span>[</span>nb 46<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="2011.E2.80.93present">2011–present</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Paul_McCartney_-_ON_THE_RUN_-_Uruguay,_2012-04-16_(3).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1365" data-file-width="2048" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/65/Paul_McCartney_-_ON_THE_RUN_-_Uruguay%2C_2012-04-16_%283%29.jpg/220px-Paul_McCartney_-_ON_THE_RUN_-_Uruguay%2C_2012-04-16_%283%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/65/Paul_McCartney_-_ON_THE_RUN_-_Uruguay%2C_2012-04-16_%283%29.jpg/330px-Paul_McCartney_-_ON_THE_RUN_-_Uruguay%2C_2012-04-16_%283%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/65/Paul_McCartney_-_ON_THE_RUN_-_Uruguay%2C_2012-04-16_%283%29.jpg/440px-Paul_McCartney_-_ON_THE_RUN_-_Uruguay%2C_2012-04-16_%283%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Paul_McCartney_-_ON_THE_RUN_-_Uruguay,_2012-04-16_(3).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Paul McCartney - On The Run - Uruguay, 2012</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In July 2011, McCartney played two sold-out concerts at the new <a href="/wiki/Yankee_Stadium" title="Yankee Stadium">Yankee Stadium</a>. A <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/New_York_Times" title="New York Times">New York Times</a></i> review of the first concert reported that McCartney was "not saying goodbye but touring stadiums and playing marathon concerts."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-235"><a href="#cite_note-235"><span>[</span>189<span>]</span></a></sup> In September 2011, having been commissioned by the <a href="/wiki/New_York_City_Ballet" title="New York City Ballet">New York City Ballet</a>, McCartney released his first score for dance, a collaboration with <a href="/wiki/Peter_Martins" title="Peter Martins">Peter Martins</a> called <i><a href="/wiki/Ocean%27s_Kingdom" title="Ocean's Kingdom">Ocean's Kingdom</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-236"><a href="#cite_note-236"><span>[</span>190<span>]</span></a></sup> Also in 2011, McCartney married Nancy Shevell.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BBC_News_237-0"><a href="#cite_note-BBC_News-237"><span>[</span>191<span>]</span></a></sup> He released <i><a href="/wiki/Kisses_on_the_Bottom" title="Kisses on the Bottom">Kisses on the Bottom</a></i>, a collection of <a href="/wiki/Standard_(music)" title="Standard (music)">standards</a>, in February 2012; that same month the <a href="/wiki/National_Academy_of_Recording_Arts_and_Sciences" title="National Academy of Recording Arts and Sciences">National Academy of Recording Arts and Sciences</a> honoured him as the <a href="/wiki/MusiCares_Person_of_the_Year" title="MusiCares Person of the Year">MusiCares Person of the Year</a>, two days prior to his performance at the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/54th_Grammy_Awards" title="54th Grammy Awards">54th Grammy Awards</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-238"><a href="#cite_note-238"><span>[</span>192<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>As of 2013<sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Paul_McCartney&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, McCartney remains one of the world's top draws. He played to over 100,000 people total during two performances in <a href="/wiki/Mexico_City" title="Mexico City">Mexico City</a> in May, the shows grossing nearly $6 million.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-239"><a href="#cite_note-239"><span>[</span>193<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-241"><a href="#cite_note-241"><span>[</span>nb 47<span>]</span></a></sup> In June 2012, McCartney closed Queen Elizabeth's <a href="/wiki/Diamond_Jubilee_Concert" title="Diamond Jubilee Concert">Diamond Jubilee Concert</a> held outside <a href="/wiki/Buckingham_Palace" title="Buckingham Palace">Buckingham Palace</a>, performing a set that included "Let It Be" and "Live and Let Die".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-242"><a href="#cite_note-242"><span>[</span>195<span>]</span></a></sup> He closed the <a href="/wiki/2012_Summer_Olympics_opening_ceremony" title="2012 Summer Olympics opening ceremony">opening ceremony</a> of the <a href="/wiki/2012_Summer_Olympics" title="2012 Summer Olympics">2012 Summer Olympics</a> in London on 27 July, singing "<a href="/wiki/The_End_(Beatles_song)" title="The End (Beatles song)">The End</a>" and "<a href="/wiki/Hey_Jude" title="Hey Jude">Hey Jude</a>" and inviting the audience to join in on the <a href="/wiki/Coda_(music)" title="Coda (music)">coda</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-243"><a href="#cite_note-243"><span>[</span>196<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Paul_McCartney,_2011_04.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2430" data-file-width="1720" height="311" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f0/Paul_McCartney%2C_2011_04.jpg/220px-Paul_McCartney%2C_2011_04.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f0/Paul_McCartney%2C_2011_04.jpg/330px-Paul_McCartney%2C_2011_04.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f0/Paul_McCartney%2C_2011_04.jpg/440px-Paul_McCartney%2C_2011_04.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Paul_McCartney,_2011_04.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Paul McCartney, 2011</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Having donated his time, he received £1 from the Olympic organisers.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-244"><a href="#cite_note-244"><span>[</span>197<span>]</span></a></sup> On 12 December, McCartney performed with three former members of <a href="/wiki/Nirvana_(band)" title="Nirvana (band)">Nirvana</a>: <a href="/wiki/Krist_Novoselic" title="Krist Novoselic">Krist Novoselic</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dave_Grohl" title="Dave Grohl">Dave Grohl</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Pat_Smear" title="Pat Smear">Pat Smear</a> during the closing act of <a href="/wiki/12-12-12:_The_Concert_for_Sandy_Relief" title="12-12-12: The Concert for Sandy Relief">12-12-12: The Concert for Sandy Relief</a>, seen by approximately two billion people worldwide.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-245"><a href="#cite_note-245"><span>[</span>198<span>]</span></a></sup> On 28 August 2013, McCartney released the title track of his upcoming studio album <i><a href="/wiki/New_(album)" title="New (album)">New</a></i>, which came out in October 2013.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-246"><a href="#cite_note-246"><span>[</span>199<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>A primetime entertainment special celebrating the legacy of seven-time Grammy-winning group the Beatles and their groundbreaking first performance on <i>The Ed Sullivan Show</i>, featuring Paul McCartney and Ringo Starr, was taped 27 January 2014 at the Ed Sullivan Theater with a 9 February 2014 CBS airing. The show, titled <i><a href="/wiki/The_Night_That_Changed_America:_A_Grammy_Salute_to_The_Beatles" title="The Night That Changed America: A Grammy Salute to The Beatles">The Night That Changed America: A Grammy Salute to The Beatles</a></i>, featured 22 classic Beatles songs as performed by various artists, including McCartney and Starr.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-247"><a href="#cite_note-247"><span>[</span>200<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>On 19 May 2014, it was reported that McCartney had been bedridden by an unspecified virus on doctor's orders, and had to cancel a sold-out concert tour of Japan scheduled to begin later in the week. The tour would have included a stop at the famed Budokan Hall. McCartney also had to push his June US dates to October, as part of his doctor's order to take it easy to make a full recovery.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-248"><a href="#cite_note-248"><span>[</span>201<span>]</span></a></sup> However, he resumed the tour with a high-energy three hour appearance in Albany, New York, on 5 July 2014.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-RSAlbany_249-0"><a href="#cite_note-RSAlbany-249"><span>[</span>202<span>]</span></a></sup> On 14 August 2014, McCartney performed the final concert at <a href="/wiki/Candlestick_Park" title="Candlestick Park">Candlestick Park</a> in <a href="/wiki/San_Francisco" title="San Francisco">San Francisco</a>, California before its demolition. It was the same venue that the Beatles played their final concert in 1966.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-250"><a href="#cite_note-250"><span>[</span>203<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>In 2014, McCartney wrote and performed <i>Hope for the Future</i>, the ending song for the video game <i><a href="/wiki/Destiny_(video_game)" title="Destiny (video game)">Destiny</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Music_251-0"><a href="#cite_note-Music-251"><span>[</span>204<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-252"><a href="#cite_note-252"><span>[</span>205<span>]</span></a></sup> In November 2014, a 42-song tribute album titled <i><a href="/wiki/The_Art_of_McCartney" title="The Art of McCartney">The Art of McCartney</a></i> was released, which features a wide range of artists covering McCartney's solo and Beatles work.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-253"><a href="#cite_note-253"><span>[</span>206<span>]</span></a></sup> Also that year, McCartney collaborated with American recording artist <a href="/wiki/Kanye_West" title="Kanye West">Kanye West</a> on the single <a href="/wiki/Only_One_(Kanye_West_song)" title="Only One (Kanye West song)">Only One</a>, released on 31 December.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-254"><a href="#cite_note-254"><span>[</span>207<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Musicianship">Musicianship</span></h2>
<p>Largely a self-taught musician, McCartney's approach was described by musicologist Ian MacDonald as "by nature drawn to music's formal aspects yet wholly untutored ... [he] produced technically 'finished' work almost entirely by instinct, his harmonic judgement based mainly on perfect pitch and an acute pair of ears ... [A] natural melodist—a creator of tunes capable of existing apart from their harmony".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-255"><a href="#cite_note-255"><span>[</span>208<span>]</span></a></sup> McCartney commented, "I prefer to think of my approach to music as ... rather like the primitive cave artists, who drew without training."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBenitez2010134_256-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBenitez2010134-256"><span>[</span>209<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Bass_guitar">Bass guitar</span></h3>
<p>McCartney's skill as a bass player has been acknowledged by other bassists, including <a href="/wiki/Sting_(musician)" title="Sting (musician)">Sting</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dr._Dre" title="Dr. Dre">Dr. Dre</a> bassist <a href="/wiki/Mike_Elizondo" title="Mike Elizondo">Mike Elizondo</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Colin_Moulding" title="Colin Moulding">Colin Moulding</a> of <a href="/wiki/XTC" title="XTC">XTC</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBaconMorgan20068_257-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBaconMorgan20068-257"><span>[</span>210<span>]</span></a></sup> Best known for primarily using a <a href="/wiki/Plectrum" title="Plectrum">plectrum</a> or <a href="/wiki/Guitar_pick" title="Guitar pick">pick</a>, McCartney occasionally plays fingerstyle.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBaconMorgan200628_258-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBaconMorgan200628-258"><span>[</span>211<span>]</span></a></sup> He does not use <a href="/wiki/Slapping_(music)" title="Slapping (music)">slapping</a> or muting techniques.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEJisi200542_259-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEJisi200542-259"><span>[</span>212<span>]</span></a></sup> He was strongly influenced by <a href="/wiki/Motown" title="Motown">Motown</a> artists, in particular <a href="/wiki/James_Jamerson" title="James Jamerson">James Jamerson</a>, who McCartney called a hero for his <a href="/wiki/Melody" title="Melody">melodic</a> style. He was also influenced by <a href="/wiki/Brian_Wilson" title="Brian Wilson">Brian Wilson</a>, as he commented: "because he went to very unusual places".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBaconMorgan200638.E2.80.9339_260-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBaconMorgan200638.E2.80.9339-260"><span>[</span>213<span>]</span></a></sup> Another favourite bassist of his is <a href="/wiki/Stanley_Clarke" title="Stanley Clarke">Stanley Clarke</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-261"><a href="#cite_note-261"><span>[</span>214<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<div class="quotebox" style="float: right; clear: right; margin: 0.5em 0 0.8em 1.4em; width:25%; padding: 6px; border: 1px solid #aaa; font-size: 88%; background-color: #F9F9F9; padding:8px;">
<div class="" style="position: relative; text-align: left;">
<div>
<p>"Paul is one of the most innovative bass players ... half the stuff that's going on now is directly ripped off from his Beatles period ... He's an egomaniac about everything else, but his bass playing he'd always been a bit coy about."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESheffGolson1981142_262-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESheffGolson1981142-262"><span>[</span>215<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
</div>
</div>
<div style="text-align: left;">—Lennon, <i>Playboy</i> magazine, January 1981</div>
</div>
<p>During McCartney's early years with the Beatles, he primarily used a <a href="/wiki/H%C3%B6fner_500/1" title="Höfner 500/1">Höfner 500/1</a> bass, though in 1965, he began sporadically using a <a href="/wiki/Rickenbacker_4001" title="Rickenbacker 4001">Rickenbacker 4001</a>S for recording. While typically using <a href="/wiki/Vox_(musical_equipment)" title="Vox (musical equipment)">Vox amplifiers</a>, by 1967 he had also begun using a <a href="/wiki/Fender_Bassman" title="Fender Bassman">Fender Bassman</a> for amplification.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-263"><a href="#cite_note-263"><span>[</span>216<span>]</span></a></sup> During the late 1980s and early 1990s, he used a <a href="/wiki/Wal_(bass)" title="Wal (bass)">Wal 5-String</a>, which he said made him play more thick-sounding <a href="/wiki/Bassline" title="Bassline">basslines</a>, in contrast to the much lighter Höfner, which inspired him to play more sensitively, something he considers fundamental to his playing style.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEJisi200542_259-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEJisi200542-259"><span>[</span>212<span>]</span></a></sup> He changed back to the Höfner around 1990 for that reason.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEJisi200542_259-2"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEJisi200542-259"><span>[</span>212<span>]</span></a></sup> He uses <a href="/wiki/Mesa_Boogie#Bass_amps" title="Mesa Boogie">Mesa Boogie</a> bass amplifiers while performing live.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMulhern199019_264-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMulhern199019-264"><span>[</span>217<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>MacDonald identified "<a href="/wiki/She%27s_a_Woman" title="She's a Woman">She's a Woman</a>" as the turning point when McCartney's bass playing began to evolve dramatically, and Beatles biographer Chris Ingham singled out <i>Rubber Soul</i> as the moment when McCartney's playing exhibited significant progress, particularly on "<a href="/wiki/The_Word_(song)" title="The Word (song)">The Word</a>".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-265"><a href="#cite_note-265"><span>[</span>218<span>]</span></a></sup> Bacon and Morgan agreed, calling McCartney's <a href="/wiki/Groove_(music)" title="Groove (music)">groove</a> on the track "a high point in pop bass playing and ... the first proof on a recording of his serious technical ability on the instrument."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-266"><a href="#cite_note-266"><span>[</span>219<span>]</span></a></sup> MacDonald inferred the influence of <a href="/wiki/James_Brown" title="James Brown">James Brown</a>'s "<a href="/wiki/Papa%27s_Got_a_Brand_New_Bag" title="Papa's Got a Brand New Bag">Papa's Got a Brand New Bag</a>" and Pickett's "<a href="/wiki/In_the_Midnight_Hour" title="In the Midnight Hour">In the Midnight Hour</a>", American <a href="/wiki/Soul_music" title="Soul music">soul</a> tracks from which McCartney absorbed elements and drew inspiration as he "delivered his most spontaneous bass-part to date".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMacDonald2005178.E2.80.93180_267-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMacDonald2005178.E2.80.93180-267"><span>[</span>220<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Bacon and Morgan described his bassline for the Beatles song "Rain" as "an astonishing piece of playing ... [McCartney] thinking in terms of both rhythm and 'lead bass' ... [choosing] the area of the neck ... he correctly perceives will give him clarity for melody without rendering his sound too thin for groove."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBaconMorgan2006112.E2.80.93113_268-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBaconMorgan2006112.E2.80.93113-268"><span>[</span>221<span>]</span></a></sup> MacDonald considered the track the Beatles' best B-side, stating that its "clangorously saturated texture resonates around McCartney's [bassline]", which MacDonald described as "so inventive that it threatens to overwhelm the track". MacDonald also indicated the influence of <a href="/wiki/Indian_classical_music" title="Indian classical music">Indian classical music</a> in "exotic <a href="/wiki/Melisma" title="Melisma">melismas</a> in the bass part".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-269"><a href="#cite_note-269"><span>[</span>222<span>]</span></a></sup> McCartney identified <i>Sgt. Pepper's Lonely Hearts Club Band</i> as containing his strongest and most inventive bass playing, particularly on "<a href="/wiki/Lucy_in_the_Sky_with_Diamonds" title="Lucy in the Sky with Diamonds">Lucy in the Sky with Diamonds</a>".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEJisi200545.E2.80.9346_270-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEJisi200545.E2.80.9346-270"><span>[</span>223<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Acoustic_guitar">Acoustic guitar</span></h3>
<div class="quotebox" style="float: right; clear: right; margin: 0.5em 0 0.8em 1.4em; width:25%; padding: 6px; border: 1px solid #aaa; font-size: 88%; background-color: #F9F9F9; padding:8px;">
<div class="" style="position: relative; text-align: left;">
<div>
<p>"If I couldn't have any other instrument, I would have to have an acoustic guitar."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMulhern199022_271-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMulhern199022-271"><span>[</span>224<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
</div>
</div>
<div style="text-align: left;">—McCartney, <i>Guitar Player</i>, July 1990</div>
</div>
<p>McCartney primarily <a href="/wiki/Flatpicking" title="Flatpicking">flatpicks</a> while playing <a href="/wiki/Acoustic_guitar" title="Acoustic guitar">acoustic guitar</a>, though he also uses elements of <a href="/wiki/Fingerstyle_guitar" title="Fingerstyle guitar">fingerpicking</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMulhern199022_271-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMulhern199022-271"><span>[</span>224<span>]</span></a></sup> Examples of his acoustic guitar playing on Beatles tracks include "Yesterday", "I'm Looking Through You", "<a href="/wiki/Michelle_(song)" title="Michelle (song)">Michelle</a>", "<a href="/wiki/Blackbird_(Beatles_song)" title="Blackbird (Beatles song)">Blackbird</a>", "<a href="/wiki/I_Will" title="I Will">I Will</a>", "<a href="/wiki/Mother_Nature%27s_Son" title="Mother Nature's Son">Mother Nature's Son</a>" and "<a href="/wiki/Rocky_Raccoon" title="Rocky Raccoon">Rocky Raccoon</a>".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-272"><a href="#cite_note-272"><span>[</span>225<span>]</span></a></sup> McCartney singled out "Blackbird" as a personal favourite and described his technique for the guitar part in the following way: "I got my own little sort of cheating way of [fingerpicking] ... I'm actually sort of pulling two strings at a time ... I was trying to emulate those <a href="/wiki/Folk_music" title="Folk music">folk</a> players."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMulhern199022_271-2"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMulhern199022-271"><span>[</span>224<span>]</span></a></sup> He employed a similar technique for "<a href="/wiki/Jenny_Wren" title="Jenny Wren">Jenny Wren</a>".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMolenda200579_273-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMolenda200579-273"><span>[</span>226<span>]</span></a></sup> He played an <a href="/wiki/Epiphone_Texan" title="Epiphone Texan">Epiphone Texan</a> on many of his acoustic recordings, but also used a <a href="/wiki/C._F._Martin_%26_Company#Six-string_guitars" title="C. F. Martin &amp; Company">Martin D-28</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-274"><a href="#cite_note-274"><span>[</span>227<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Electric_guitar">Electric guitar</span></h3>
<div class="quotebox" style="float: right; clear: right; margin: 0.5em 0 0.8em 1.4em; width:20%; padding: 6px; border: 1px solid #aaa; font-size: 88%; background-color: #F9F9F9; padding:8px;">
<div class="" style="position: relative; text-align: left;">
<div>
<p>"Linda was a big fan of my guitar playing, whereas I've got my doubts. I think there are proper guitar players and then there are guys like me who love playing it".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMulhern199023_275-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMulhern199023-275"><span>[</span>228<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
</div>
</div>
<div style="text-align: left;">—McCartney, <i>Guitar Player</i>, July 1990</div>
</div>
<p>McCartney played lead guitar on several Beatles recordings, including what MacDonald described as a "fiercely angular slide guitar solo" on "<a href="/wiki/Drive_My_Car" title="Drive My Car">Drive My Car</a>", which McCartney played on an <a href="/wiki/Epiphone_Casino" title="Epiphone Casino">Epiphone Casino</a>. McCartney said of the instrument, "if I had to pick one electric guitar it would be this."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-276"><a href="#cite_note-276"><span>[</span>229<span>]</span></a></sup> He contributed what MacDonald described as "a startling guitar solo" on the Harrison composition "<a href="/wiki/Taxman" title="Taxman">Taxman</a>" and the "shrieking" guitar on "Sgt. Pepper's Lonely Hearts Club Band" and "<a href="/wiki/Helter_Skelter_(song)" title="Helter Skelter (song)">Helter Skelter</a>". MacDonald also praised McCartney's "coruscating pseudo-Indian" guitar solo on "<a href="/wiki/Good_Morning_Good_Morning" title="Good Morning Good Morning">Good Morning Good Morning</a>".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-277"><a href="#cite_note-277"><span>[</span>230<span>]</span></a></sup> McCartney also played lead guitar on "<a href="/wiki/Another_Girl" title="Another Girl">Another Girl</a>".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMacDonald2005145_278-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMacDonald2005145-278"><span>[</span>231<span>]</span></a></sup> On his "Taxman" solo, McCartney commented, "I was very inspired by <a href="/wiki/Jimi_Hendrix" title="Jimi Hendrix">Jimi Hendrix</a>. It was really my first voyage into <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Guitar_feedback" title="Guitar feedback">feedback</a>."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMulhern199022_271-3"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMulhern199022-271"><span>[</span>224<span>]</span></a></sup> In 1990, when asked who his favourite guitar players were he included <a href="/wiki/Eddie_Van_Halen" title="Eddie Van Halen">Eddie Van Halen</a>, <a href="/wiki/Eric_Clapton" title="Eric Clapton">Eric Clapton</a> and David Gilmour, stating, "but I still like Hendrix the best".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMulhern199022_271-4"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMulhern199022-271"><span>[</span>224<span>]</span></a></sup> He has primarily used a <a href="/wiki/Gibson_Les_Paul" title="Gibson Les Paul">Gibson Les Paul</a> for electric work, particularly during live performances.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMulhern199019_264-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMulhern199019-264"><span>[</span>217<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Vocals">Vocals</span></h3>
<p>McCartney's vocals cross several <a href="/wiki/Music_genre" title="Music genre">musical genres</a>. On "<a href="/wiki/Call_Me_Back_Again" title="Call Me Back Again">Call Me Back Again</a>", according to Benitez, "McCartney shines as a <a href="/wiki/Blues" title="Blues">bluesy</a> solo vocalist" while MacDonald called "<a href="/wiki/I%27m_Down" title="I'm Down">I'm Down</a>" "a <a href="/wiki/Rock_and_roll" title="Rock and roll">rock-and-roll</a> classic" that "illustrates McCartney's vocal and stylistic versatility".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-279"><a href="#cite_note-279"><span>[</span>232<span>]</span></a></sup> MacDonald described "Helter Skelter" as an early attempt at <a href="/wiki/Heavy_metal_music" title="Heavy metal music">heavy metal</a>, and "Hey Jude" as a "<a href="/wiki/Pop_music" title="Pop music">pop</a>/rock hybrid", pointing out McCartney's "use of <a href="/wiki/Gospel_music" title="Gospel music">gospel</a>-style <a href="/wiki/Melisma" title="Melisma">melismas</a>" in the song and his "pseudo-<a href="/wiki/Soul_music" title="Soul music">soul</a> shrieking in the fade-out".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-280"><a href="#cite_note-280"><span>[</span>233<span>]</span></a></sup> Benitez identified "<a href="/wiki/Hope_of_Deliverance" title="Hope of Deliverance">Hope of Deliverance</a>" and "<a href="/wiki/Put_It_There" title="Put It There">Put It There</a>" as examples of McCartney's folk music efforts while musicologist <a href="/wiki/Walter_Everett_(musicologist)" title="Walter Everett (musicologist)">Walter Everett</a> considered "<a href="/wiki/When_I%27m_Sixty-Four" title="When I'm Sixty-Four">When I'm Sixty-Four</a>" and "<a href="/wiki/Honey_Pie" title="Honey Pie">Honey Pie</a>" attempts at <a href="/wiki/Vaudeville" title="Vaudeville">vaudeville</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-281"><a href="#cite_note-281"><span>[</span>234<span>]</span></a></sup> MacDonald praised the "<a href="/wiki/Swing_music" title="Swing music">swinging</a> beat" of the Beatles' <a href="/wiki/Twelve-bar_blues" title="Twelve-bar blues">twenty-four bar blues</a> song, "She's a Woman" as "the most extreme sound they had manufactured to date", with McCartney's voice "at the edge, squeezed to the upper limit of his chest register and threatening to crack at any moment."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMacDonald2005133.E2.80.93134_282-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMacDonald2005133.E2.80.93134-282"><span>[</span>235<span>]</span></a></sup> MacDonald described "<a href="/wiki/I%27ve_Got_a_Feeling" title="I've Got a Feeling">I've Got a Feeling</a>" as a "raunchy, mid-tempo rocker" with a "robust and soulful" vocal performance and "Back in the U.S.S.R." as "the last of [the Beatles'] up-tempo rockers", McCartney's "<a href="/wiki/Belting_(music)" title="Belting (music)">belting</a>" vocals among his best since "Drive My Car", recorded three years earlier.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-283"><a href="#cite_note-283"><span>[</span>236<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Keyboards">Keyboards</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Paul_McCartney_in_The_White_House.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2731" data-file-width="4096" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9a/Paul_McCartney_in_The_White_House.jpg/220px-Paul_McCartney_in_The_White_House.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9a/Paul_McCartney_in_The_White_House.jpg/330px-Paul_McCartney_in_The_White_House.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9a/Paul_McCartney_in_The_White_House.jpg/440px-Paul_McCartney_in_The_White_House.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Paul_McCartney_in_The_White_House.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Paul McCartney in The White House, 2010</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>McCartney played piano on several Beatles songs, including "<a href="/wiki/Every_Little_Thing_(Beatles_song)" title="Every Little Thing (Beatles song)">Every Little Thing</a>", "She's a Woman", "<a href="/wiki/For_No_One" title="For No One">For No One</a>", "<a href="/wiki/A_Day_in_the_Life" title="A Day in the Life">A Day in the Life</a>", "Hello, Goodbye", "Hey Jude", "<a href="/wiki/Lady_Madonna" title="Lady Madonna">Lady Madonna</a>", "Let It Be" and "The Long and Winding Road".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-284"><a href="#cite_note-284"><span>[</span>237<span>]</span></a></sup> MacDonald considered the piano part in "Lady Madonna" as reminiscent of <a href="/wiki/Fats_Domino" title="Fats Domino">Fats Domino</a>, and "Let It Be" as having a gospel rhythm.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-285"><a href="#cite_note-285"><span>[</span>238<span>]</span></a></sup> MacDonald called McCartney's <a href="/wiki/Mellotron" title="Mellotron">Mellotron</a> intro on "<a href="/wiki/Strawberry_Fields_Forever" title="Strawberry Fields Forever">Strawberry Fields Forever</a>" an integral feature of the song's character.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMacDonald2005219_286-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMacDonald2005219-286"><span>[</span>239<span>]</span></a></sup> McCartney played a <a href="/wiki/Moog_synthesizer" title="Moog synthesizer">Moog synthesizer</a> on the Beatles song "<a href="/wiki/Maxwell%27s_Silver_Hammer" title="Maxwell's Silver Hammer">Maxwell's Silver Hammer</a>" and the Wings track "Loup (1st Indian on the Moon)".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-287"><a href="#cite_note-287"><span>[</span>240<span>]</span></a></sup> Ingham described the Wings songs "<a href="/wiki/With_a_Little_Luck" title="With a Little Luck">With a Little Luck</a>" and "<a href="/wiki/London_Town_(Wings_song)" title="London Town (Wings song)">London Town</a>" as "full of the most sensitive pop synthesizer touches".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-288"><a href="#cite_note-288"><span>[</span>241<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Drums">Drums</span></h3>
<p>McCartney played drums on the Beatles' songs "Back in the U.S.S.R.", "<a href="/wiki/Dear_Prudence" title="Dear Prudence">Dear Prudence</a>", "<a href="/wiki/Martha_My_Dear" title="Martha My Dear">Martha My Dear</a>", "<a href="/wiki/Wild_Honey_Pie" title="Wild Honey Pie">Wild Honey Pie</a>" and "<a href="/wiki/The_Ballad_of_John_and_Yoko" title="The Ballad of John and Yoko">The Ballad of John and Yoko</a>".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-289"><a href="#cite_note-289"><span>[</span>242<span>]</span></a></sup> He also played all the drum parts on his first and second solo albums <i>McCartney</i> and <i>McCartney II</i>, as well as on the Wings album <i>Band on the Run</i> and most of the drums on his solo LP <i>Chaos and Creation in the Backyard</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-290"><a href="#cite_note-290"><span>[</span>243<span>]</span></a></sup> McCartney also played drums on <a href="/wiki/Paul_Jones_(singer)" title="Paul Jones (singer)">Paul Jones</a>' rendition of "<a href="/wiki/And_the_Sun_Will_Shine#Paul_Jones_version" title="And the Sun Will Shine">And the Sun Will Shine</a>" in 1968.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-291"><a href="#cite_note-291"><span>[</span>244<span>]</span></a></sup> Using the pseudonym Paul Ramon, which he had first used during the Beatles first tour in Scotland in 1960, McCartney played drums on <a href="/wiki/Steve_Miller_Band" title="Steve Miller Band">Steve Miller Band</a>'s 1969 tracks "Celebration Song" and "My Dark Hour".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-292"><a href="#cite_note-292"><span>[</span>245<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-293"><a href="#cite_note-293"><span>[</span>246<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Tape_loops">Tape loops</span></h3>
<p>In the mid-1960s, when visiting artist friend <a href="/wiki/John_Dunbar_(artist)" title="John Dunbar (artist)">John Dunbar</a>'s flat in London, McCartney brought <a href="/wiki/Magnetic_tape" title="Magnetic tape">tapes</a> he had compiled at then-girlfriend <a href="/wiki/Jane_Asher" title="Jane Asher">Jane Asher</a>'s home. They included mixes of various songs, musical pieces and comments made by McCartney that <a href="/wiki/Dick_James" title="Dick James">Dick James</a> made into a demo for him.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMiles1997217.E2.80.93218_294-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMiles1997217.E2.80.93218-294"><span>[</span>247<span>]</span></a></sup> Heavily influenced by American <a href="/wiki/Avant-garde" title="Avant-garde">avant-garde</a> musician <a href="/wiki/John_Cage" title="John Cage">John Cage</a>, McCartney made <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tape_loops" title="Tape loops">tape loops</a> by recording voices, guitars and bongos on a <a href="/wiki/Brenell_Engineering" title="Brenell Engineering">Brenell</a> <a href="/wiki/Reel-to-reel_audio_tape_recording" title="Reel-to-reel audio tape recording">tape recorder</a> and splicing the various loops. He referred to the finished product as "electronic symphonies".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMiles1997219.E2.80.93220_295-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMiles1997219.E2.80.93220-295"><span>[</span>248<span>]</span></a></sup> He reversed the tapes, speeded them up, and slowed them down to create the desired effects, some of which the Beatles later used on the songs "<a href="/wiki/Tomorrow_Never_Knows" title="Tomorrow Never Knows">Tomorrow Never Knows</a>" and "<a href="/wiki/The_Fool_on_the_Hill" title="The Fool on the Hill">The Fool on the Hill</a>".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-296"><a href="#cite_note-296"><span>[</span>249<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_influences">Early influences</span></h3>
<div class="quotebox" style="float: right; clear: right; margin: 0.5em 0 0.8em 1.4em; width:20%; padding: 6px; border: 1px solid #aaa; font-size: 88%; background-color: #F9F9F9; padding:8px;">
<div class="" style="position: relative; text-align: left;">
<div>
<p>"The <a href="/wiki/Messiah" title="Messiah">Messiah</a> has arrived!"<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-297"><a href="#cite_note-297"><span>[</span>250<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
</div>
</div>
<div style="text-align: left;">—McCartney on Presley, <i>The Beatles Anthology</i>, 2000</div>
</div>
<p>McCartney's earliest musical influences include <a href="/wiki/Little_Richard" title="Little Richard">Little Richard</a>, <a href="/wiki/Elvis_Presley" title="Elvis Presley">Elvis Presley</a>, <a href="/wiki/Buddy_Holly" title="Buddy Holly">Buddy Holly</a>, <a href="/wiki/Carl_Perkins" title="Carl Perkins">Carl Perkins</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Chuck_Berry" title="Chuck Berry">Chuck Berry</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-298"><a href="#cite_note-298"><span>[</span>251<span>]</span></a></sup> When asked why the Beatles did not include Presley on the <i>Sgt. Pepper</i> cover, McCartney replied, "Elvis was too important and too far above the rest even to mention ... so we didn't put him on the list because he was more than merely a ... pop singer, he was Elvis the King."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHarry2002727_299-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHarry2002727-299"><span>[</span>252<span>]</span></a></sup> McCartney stated that for his bassline for "<a href="/wiki/I_Saw_Her_Standing_There" title="I Saw Her Standing There">I Saw Her Standing There</a>", he directly quoted Berry's "<a href="/wiki/I%27m_Talking_About_You" title="I'm Talking About You">I'm Talking About You</a>".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-300"><a href="#cite_note-300"><span>[</span>253<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>McCartney called Little Richard an idol, whose <a href="/wiki/Falsetto" title="Falsetto">falsetto</a> <a href="/wiki/Vocal_music" title="Vocal music">vocalisations</a> inspired McCartney's own vocal technique.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMulhern199033_301-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMulhern199033-301"><span>[</span>254<span>]</span></a></sup> McCartney said he wrote "I'm Down" as a vehicle for his Little Richard impersonation.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-302"><a href="#cite_note-302"><span>[</span>255<span>]</span></a></sup> In 1971, McCartney bought the publishing rights to Holly's catalogue, and in 1976, on the fortieth anniversary of Holly's birth, McCartney inaugurated the annual "Buddy Holly Week" in England. The festival has included guest performances by famous musicians, songwriting competitions, drawing contests and special events featuring performances by <a href="/wiki/The_Crickets" title="The Crickets">the Crickets</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-303"><a href="#cite_note-303"><span>[</span>256<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Lifestyle">Lifestyle</span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Creative_outlets">Creative outlets</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Mccartney_gershwin.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="356" data-file-width="635" height="123" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5f/Mccartney_gershwin.png/220px-Mccartney_gershwin.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5f/Mccartney_gershwin.png/330px-Mccartney_gershwin.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5f/Mccartney_gershwin.png/440px-Mccartney_gershwin.png 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Mccartney_gershwin.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Paul McCartney receiving the Gershwin Award from Barack Obama</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>While at school during the 1950s, McCartney thrived at art assignments, often earning top accolades for his visual work. However, his lack of discipline negatively affected his academic grades, preventing him from earning admission to art college.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECarlin200944.E2.80.9345_304-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECarlin200944.E2.80.9345-304"><span>[</span>257<span>]</span></a></sup> During the 1960s, he delved into the visual arts, explored experimental cinema, and regularly attended film, theatrical and classical music performances. His first contact with the London <a href="/wiki/Avant-garde" title="Avant-garde">avant-garde</a> scene was through artist <a href="/wiki/John_Dunbar_(artist)" title="John Dunbar (artist)">John Dunbar</a>, who introduced McCartney to art dealer <a href="/wiki/Robert_Fraser_(art_dealer)" title="Robert Fraser (art dealer)">Robert Fraser</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHarry2002307_305-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHarry2002307-305"><span>[</span>258<span>]</span></a></sup> At Fraser's flat he first learned about art appreciation and met <a href="/wiki/Andy_Warhol" title="Andy Warhol">Andy Warhol</a>, <a href="/wiki/Claes_Oldenburg" title="Claes Oldenburg">Claes Oldenburg</a>, <a href="/wiki/Peter_Blake_(artist)" title="Peter Blake (artist)">Peter Blake</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Richard_Hamilton_(artist)" title="Richard Hamilton (artist)">Richard Hamilton</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMiles1997243_306-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMiles1997243-306"><span>[</span>259<span>]</span></a></sup> McCartney later purchased works by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Magritte" title="Magritte">Magritte</a>, using his painting of an apple for the <a href="/wiki/Apple_Records" title="Apple Records">Apple Records</a> logo.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMiles1997256.E2.80.93267_307-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMiles1997256.E2.80.93267-307"><span>[</span>260<span>]</span></a></sup> McCartney became involved in the renovation and publicising of the <a href="/wiki/Indica_Gallery" title="Indica Gallery">Indica Gallery</a> in Mason's Yard, London, which <a href="/wiki/Barry_Miles" title="Barry Miles">Barry Miles</a> had co-founded and where Lennon first met <a href="/wiki/Yoko_Ono" title="Yoko Ono">Yoko Ono</a>. Miles also co-founded <i><a href="/wiki/International_Times" title="International Times">International Times</a></i>, an underground paper that McCartney helped to start with direct financial support and by providing interviews to attract advertiser income. Miles later wrote McCartney's official biography, <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Many_Years_From_Now" title="Many Years From Now">Many Years From Now</a></i> (1997).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-308"><a href="#cite_note-308"><span>[</span>261<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>McCartney became interested in painting after watching artist <a href="/wiki/Willem_de_Kooning" title="Willem de Kooning">Willem de Kooning</a> work in de Kooning's <a href="/wiki/Long_Island" title="Long Island">Long Island</a> studio.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESpitz200584_309-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESpitz200584-309"><span>[</span>262<span>]</span></a></sup> McCartney took up painting in 1983, and he first exhibited his work in <a href="/wiki/Siegen" title="Siegen">Siegen</a>, Germany, in 1999. The 70-painting show featured portraits of Lennon, <a href="/wiki/Andy_Warhol" title="Andy Warhol">Andy Warhol</a> and <a href="/wiki/David_Bowie" title="David Bowie">David Bowie</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMiles1997266_310-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMiles1997266-310"><span>[</span>263<span>]</span></a></sup> Though initially reluctant to display his paintings publicly, McCartney chose the gallery because events organiser Wolfgang Suttner showed genuine interest in McCartney's art.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESounes2010453_311-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESounes2010453-311"><span>[</span>264<span>]</span></a></sup> In September 2000, the first UK exhibition of McCartney's paintings opened, featuring 500 canvases at the <a href="/wiki/Arnolfini" title="Arnolfini">Arnolfini Gallery</a> in Bristol, England.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-312"><a href="#cite_note-312"><span>[</span>265<span>]</span></a></sup> In October 2000, McCartney's art debuted in his hometown of Liverpool. McCartney said, "I've been offered an exhibition of my paintings at the Walker Art Gallery ... where John and I used to spend many a pleasant afternoon. So I'm really excited about it. I didn't tell anybody I painted for 15 years but now I'm out of the closet".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-313"><a href="#cite_note-313"><span>[</span>266<span>]</span></a></sup> McCartney is lead patron of the <a href="/wiki/Liverpool_Institute_for_Performing_Arts" title="Liverpool Institute for Performing Arts">Liverpool Institute for Performing Arts</a>, a school in the building formerly occupied by the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Liverpool_Institute_for_Boys" title="Liverpool Institute for Boys">Liverpool Institute for Boys</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHarry2002517.E2.80.93526_314-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHarry2002517.E2.80.93526-314"><span>[</span>267<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>When McCartney was a child, his mother read him poems and encouraged him to read books. His father invited Paul and his brother Michael to solve <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Crosswords" title="Crosswords">crosswords</a> with him, to increase their "word power", as McCartney said.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-315"><a href="#cite_note-315"><span>[</span>268<span>]</span></a></sup> In 2001, McCartney published <i>Blackbird Singing</i>, a volume of poems and lyrics to his songs for which he gave readings in Liverpool and New York City.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FaberandFaber_316-0"><a href="#cite_note-FaberandFaber-316"><span>[</span>269<span>]</span></a></sup> In the foreword of the book, he explains: "When I was a teenager ... I had an overwhelming desire to have a poem published in the school magazine. I wrote something deep and meaningful—which was promptly rejected—and I suppose I have been trying to get my own back ever since".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMcCartneyMitchell200113_317-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMcCartneyMitchell200113-317"><span>[</span>270<span>]</span></a></sup> His first children's book was published by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Faber_%26_Faber" title="Faber &amp; Faber">Faber &amp; Faber</a> in 2005, <i><a href="/wiki/High_in_the_Clouds" title="High in the Clouds">High in the Clouds: An Urban Furry Tail</a></i>, a collaboration with writer <a href="/wiki/Philip_Ardagh" title="Philip Ardagh">Philip Ardagh</a> and animator Geoff Dunbar. Featuring a squirrel whose woodland home is razed by developers, it had been scripted and sketched by McCartney and Dunbar over several years, as an animated film. <i><a href="/wiki/The_Observer" title="The Observer">The Observer</a></i> labelled it an "anti-capitalist children's book".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-318"><a href="#cite_note-318"><span>[</span>271<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<div class="quotebox" style="float: right; clear: right; margin: 0.5em 0 0.8em 1.4em; width:25%; padding: 6px; border: 1px solid #aaa; font-size: 88%; background-color: #F9F9F9; padding:8px;">
<div class="" style="position: relative; text-align: left;">
<div>
<p>"I think there's an urge in us to stop the terrible fleetingness of time. Music. Paintings ... Try and capture one bloody moment please."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEIngham2009219_319-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEIngham2009219-319"><span>[</span>272<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
</div>
</div>
<div style="text-align: left;">—McCartney</div>
</div>
<p>In 1981, McCartney asked Geoff Dunbar to direct a short <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Animated_film" title="Animated film">animated film</a> called <i><a href="/wiki/Rupert_and_the_Frog_Song" title="Rupert and the Frog Song">Rupert and the Frog Song</a></i>; McCartney was the writer and producer, and he also added some of the character voices.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHarry2002767_320-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHarry2002767-320"><span>[</span>273<span>]</span></a></sup> In 1992, he worked with Dunbar on an animated film about the work of French artist <a href="/wiki/Honor%C3%A9_Daumier" title="Honoré Daumier">Honoré Daumier</a>, which won them a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/BAFTA" title="BAFTA">BAFTA</a> award.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Animatedfilm1992_321-0"><a href="#cite_note-Animatedfilm1992-321"><span>[</span>274<span>]</span></a></sup> In 2004, they worked together on the animated short film <i><a href="/wiki/Tropic_Island_Hum" title="Tropic Island Hum">Tropic Island Hum</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHarry2002862_322-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHarry2002862-322"><span>[</span>275<span>]</span></a></sup> The accompanying single, "Tropic Island Hum"/"<a href="/wiki/We_All_Stand_Together" title="We All Stand Together">We All Stand Together</a>", reached number 21 in the UK.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBlaney2007266_323-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBlaney2007266-323"><span>[</span>276<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>McCartney also produced and hosted <i>The Real Buddy Holly Story</i>, a 1985 documentary featuring interviews with <a href="/wiki/Keith_Richards" title="Keith Richards">Keith Richards</a>, <a href="/wiki/The_Everly_Brothers" title="The Everly Brothers">Phil and Don Everly</a>, the Holly family, and others.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-324"><a href="#cite_note-324"><span>[</span>277<span>]</span></a></sup> In 1995, he made a guest appearance on the <i><a href="/wiki/The_Simpsons" title="The Simpsons">Simpsons</a></i> episode "<a href="/wiki/Lisa_the_Vegetarian" title="Lisa the Vegetarian">Lisa the Vegetarian</a>" and directed a short documentary about the <a href="/wiki/Grateful_Dead" title="Grateful Dead">Grateful Dead</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHarry2002386.E2.80.93387:_the_Grateful_Dead_documentary.2C_789:_.22Lisa_the_Vegetarian.22.2C_862_325-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHarry2002386.E2.80.93387:_the_Grateful_Dead_documentary.2C_789:_.22Lisa_the_Vegetarian.22.2C_862-325"><span>[</span>278<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Business">Business</span></h3>
<p>Since the Rich List began in 1989, McCartney has been the UK's wealthiest musician, with an estimated fortune of £680 million in 2013.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-RL2013_326-0"><a href="#cite_note-RL2013-326"><span>[</span>279<span>]</span></a></sup> In addition to an interest in Apple Corps and <a href="/wiki/MPL_Communications" title="MPL Communications">MPL Communications</a>, an umbrella company for his business interests, he owns a significant <a href="/wiki/Music_publisher_(popular_music)" title="Music publisher (popular music)">music publishing</a> catalogue, with access to over 25,000 copyrights, including the publishing rights to the musicals <i><a href="/wiki/Guys_and_Dolls" title="Guys and Dolls">Guys and Dolls</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/A_Chorus_Line" title="A Chorus Line">A Chorus Line</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Annie_(musical)" title="Annie (musical)">Annie</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Grease_(musical)" title="Grease (musical)">Grease</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-news.bbc.co.uk_327-0"><a href="#cite_note-news.bbc.co.uk-327"><span>[</span>280<span>]</span></a></sup> He earned £40 million in 2003, the highest income that year within media professions in the UK.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-McCartney_tops_media_rich_list_328-0"><a href="#cite_note-McCartney_tops_media_rich_list-328"><span>[</span>281<span>]</span></a></sup> This rose to £48.5 million by 2005.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-48_million_in_2005_329-0"><a href="#cite_note-48_million_in_2005-329"><span>[</span>282<span>]</span></a></sup> McCartney's 18-date <a href="/wiki/On_the_Run_(Paul_McCartney)" title="On the Run (Paul McCartney)">On the Run Tour</a> grossed £37 million in 2012.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-RL2013_326-1"><a href="#cite_note-RL2013-326"><span>[</span>279<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>McCartney's music has appeared on several <a href="/wiki/Record_label" title="Record label">record labels</a>. In January 1962, <a href="/wiki/Polydor_Records" title="Polydor Records">Polydor Records</a> issued the first commercially released recording of the Beatles, a single called "<a href="/wiki/My_Bonnie" title="My Bonnie">My Bonnie</a>". Credited to <a href="/wiki/Tony_Sheridan" title="Tony Sheridan">Tony Sheridan</a> and the Beat Brothers, <a href="/wiki/Decca_Records" title="Decca Records">Decca Records</a> issued the track in the UK in April 1962. The following year, <a href="/wiki/Parlophone" title="Parlophone">Parlophone</a> released the band's singles "<a href="/wiki/Please_Please_Me_(song)" title="Please Please Me (song)">Please Please Me</a>"/"<a href="/wiki/Ask_Me_Why" title="Ask Me Why">Ask Me Why</a>" and "<a href="/wiki/From_Me_to_You" title="From Me to You">From Me to You</a>"/"<a href="/wiki/Thank_You_Girl" title="Thank You Girl">Thank You Girl</a>" in the UK. <a href="/wiki/Vee-Jay_Records" title="Vee-Jay Records">Vee-Jay Records</a> released them in the US. Also that year, <a href="/wiki/Swan_Records_(jazz_label)" title="Swan Records (jazz label)">Swan Records</a> released the group's UK Parlophone single "She Loves You"/"<a href="/wiki/I%27ll_Get_You" title="I'll Get You">I'll Get You</a>" in the US. From then until July 1968, <a href="/wiki/EMI" title="EMI">EMI</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Capitol_Records" title="Capitol Records">Capitol</a> (US) and Parlophone (UK) labels released the band's music. Starting with the August 1968 release "<a href="/wiki/Hey_Jude" title="Hey Jude">Hey Jude</a>"/"<a href="/wiki/Revolution_(Beatles_song)" title="Revolution (Beatles song)">Revolution</a>", their new material would be issued with Apple <a href="/wiki/Label" title="Label">labels</a>, logos and sleeves, but with Parlophone or Capitol serial numbers.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELewisohn1992350.E2.80.93351_31-3"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELewisohn1992350.E2.80.93351-31"><span>[</span>29<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Following the break-up of the Beatles, McCartney's music continued to be released by Apple Records under the Beatles' 1967 recording contract with EMI which ran until 1976. Following the formal dissolution of the Beatles' partnership in 1975, McCartney re-signed with EMI worldwide and Capitol in the US and Canada. In 1979, McCartney signed with <a href="/wiki/Columbia_Records" title="Columbia Records">Columbia Records</a> in the US and Canada—reportedly receiving the industry's most lucrative recording contract to date, while remaining with EMI for distribution throughout the rest of the world.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMcGee2003125.E2.80.93126_330-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMcGee2003125.E2.80.93126-330"><span>[</span>283<span>]</span></a></sup> McCartney returned to Capitol in 1985 and from 1985 until 2006, Parlophone released McCartney's music in the UK and Capitol in the US.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Blaney_2007_287.E2.80.93297_331-0"><a href="#cite_note-Blaney_2007_287.E2.80.93297-331"><span>[</span>284<span>]</span></a></sup> In 2007, McCartney signed with <a href="/wiki/Hear_Music" title="Hear Music">Hear Music</a>, becoming the label's first artist. He remains there as of 2012<sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Paul_McCartney&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>'s <i><a href="/wiki/Kisses_on_the_Bottom" title="Kisses on the Bottom">Kisses on the Bottom</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rollingstone.com_332-0"><a href="#cite_note-rollingstone.com-332"><span>[</span>285<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>In 1963, <a href="/wiki/Dick_James" title="Dick James">Dick James</a> established <a href="/wiki/Northern_Songs" title="Northern Songs">Northern Songs</a> to publish the songs of Lennon–McCartney.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESpitz2005365_333-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESpitz2005365-333"><span>[</span>286<span>]</span></a></sup> McCartney initially owned 20% of Northern Songs, which became 15% after a public stock offering in 1965. In 1969, James sold a controlling interest in Northern Songs to <a href="/wiki/Lew_Grade" title="Lew Grade">Lew Grade</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Associated_Television" title="Associated Television">Associated Television</a> (ATV) after which McCartney and John Lennon sold their remaining shares although they remained under contract to ATV until 1973. In 1972, McCartney re-signed with ATV for seven years in a joint publishing agreement between ATV and <a href="/wiki/MPL_Communications" title="MPL Communications">McCartney Music</a>. Since 1979, MPL Communications has published McCartney's songs. McCartney and <a href="/wiki/Yoko_Ono" title="Yoko Ono">Yoko Ono</a> attempted to purchase the Northern Songs catalogue in 1981, but Grade declined their offer and decided to sell ATV in its entirety to businessman <a href="/wiki/Robert_Holmes_%C3%A0_Court" title="Robert Holmes à Court">Robert Holmes à Court</a>. <a href="/wiki/Michael_Jackson" title="Michael Jackson">Michael Jackson</a> subsequently purchased ATV in 1985. In 1995, Jackson merged his catalogue with Sony for a reported £59,052,000 ($95 million), establishing Sony/ATV Music Publishing, in which he retained half-ownership.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-JacksonBailout_334-0"><a href="#cite_note-JacksonBailout-334"><span>[</span>287<span>]</span></a></sup> McCartney has criticised Jackson's purchase and handling of Northern Songs over the years. Now formally dissolved, in 1995 it became absorbed in the Sony/ATV catalogue.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Harry_2002_456.E2.80.93459_335-0"><a href="#cite_note-Harry_2002_456.E2.80.93459-335"><span>[</span>288<span>]</span></a></sup> McCartney receives writers' royalties which together are 33⅓ percent of total commercial proceeds in the US, and which vary elsewhere between 50 and 55 percent.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESouthallPerry2006195_336-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESouthallPerry2006195-336"><span>[</span>289<span>]</span></a></sup> Two of the Beatles' earliest songs—"<a href="/wiki/Love_Me_Do" title="Love Me Do">Love Me Do</a>" and "<a href="/wiki/P.S._I_Love_You_(Beatles_song)" title="P.S. I Love You (Beatles song)">P.S. I Love You</a>"—were published by an EMI subsidiary, Ardmore &amp; Beechwood, before signing with James. McCartney acquired their publishing rights from Ardmore in the mid-1980s, and they are the only two Beatles songs owned by MPL Communications.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Harry_2002_536_337-0"><a href="#cite_note-Harry_2002_536-337"><span>[</span>290<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Drugs">Drugs</span></h3>
<p>McCartney first used drugs in the Beatles' <a href="/wiki/Hamburg" title="Hamburg">Hamburg</a> days, when they often used <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Preludin" title="Preludin">Preludin</a> to maintain their energy while performing for long periods.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMiles199766.E2.80.9367_338-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMiles199766.E2.80.9367-338"><span>[</span>291<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Bob_Dylan" title="Bob Dylan">Bob Dylan</a> introduced them to <a href="/wiki/Cannabis_(drug)" title="Cannabis (drug)">marijuana</a> in a New York hotel room in 1964; McCartney recalls getting "very high" and "giggling uncontrollably".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMiles1997186.E2.80.93189_339-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMiles1997186.E2.80.93189-339"><span>[</span>292<span>]</span></a></sup> His use of the drug soon became habitual, and according to Miles, McCartney wrote the lyrics "another kind of mind" in "<a href="/wiki/Got_to_Get_You_into_My_Life" title="Got to Get You into My Life">Got to Get You into My Life</a>" specifically as a reference to cannabis.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-340"><a href="#cite_note-340"><span>[</span>293<span>]</span></a></sup> During the filming of <i><a href="/wiki/Help!_(film)" title="Help! (film)">Help!</a></i>, McCartney occasionally smoked a <a href="/wiki/Joint_(cannabis)" title="Joint (cannabis)">joint</a> in the car on the way to the studio during filming, and often forgot his lines.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMiles199767.E2.80.9368_341-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMiles199767.E2.80.9368-341"><span>[</span>294<span>]</span></a></sup> Director <a href="/wiki/Richard_Lester" title="Richard Lester">Richard Lester</a> overheard two physically attractive women trying to persuade McCartney to use heroin, but he refused.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMiles199767.E2.80.9368_341-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMiles199767.E2.80.9368-341"><span>[</span>294<span>]</span></a></sup> Introduced to <a href="/wiki/Cocaine" title="Cocaine">cocaine</a> by Robert Fraser, McCartney used the drug regularly during the recording of <i>Sgt. Pepper's Lonely Hearts Club Band</i>, and for about a year total but stopped because of his dislike of the unpleasant melancholy he felt afterwards.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-342"><a href="#cite_note-342"><span>[</span>295<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Initially reluctant to try <a href="/wiki/Lysergic_acid_diethylamide" title="Lysergic acid diethylamide">LSD</a>, McCartney eventually did so in late 1966, and took his second "<a href="/wiki/Psychedelic_experience" title="Psychedelic experience">acid trip</a>" in March 1967, with Lennon, after a <i>Sgt. Pepper</i> studio session.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-343"><a href="#cite_note-343"><span>[</span>296<span>]</span></a></sup> He later became the first Beatle to discuss the drug publicly, declaring, "It opened my eyes ... [and] made me a better, more honest, more tolerant member of society."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBrownGaines2002228_344-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBrownGaines2002228-344"><span>[</span>297<span>]</span></a></sup> He made his attitude about cannabis public in 1967, when he, along with the other Beatles and Epstein, added his name to a July advertisement in <i>The Times</i>, which called for its legalisation, the release of those imprisoned for possession, and research into marijuana's medical uses.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMiles1997386.E2.80.93387_345-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMiles1997386.E2.80.93387-345"><span>[</span>298<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>In 1972, a Swedish court fined McCartney £1,000 for cannabis possession. Soon after, Scottish police found marijuana plants growing on his farm, leading to his 1973 conviction for <a href="/wiki/Cannabis_cultivation" title="Cannabis cultivation">illegal cultivation</a> and a £100 fine. As a result of his drug convictions, the US government repeatedly denied him a visa until December 1973.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-346"><a href="#cite_note-346"><span>[</span>299<span>]</span></a></sup> Arrested again for marijuana possession in 1975, in Los Angeles, Linda took the blame, and the court soon dismissed the charges. In January 1980, when Wings flew to Tokyo for a tour of Japan, customs officials found approximately 8 ounces (200 g) of cannabis in his luggage. They arrested McCartney and brought him to a local jail while the Japanese government decided what to do. After ten days, they released and deported him without charge.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHarry2002459.E2.80.93461_347-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHarry2002459.E2.80.93461-347"><span>[</span>300<span>]</span></a></sup> In 1984, while McCartney was on holiday in Barbados, authorities arrested him for possession of marijuana and fined him $200.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHarry2002300.E2.80.93307_348-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHarry2002300.E2.80.93307-348"><span>[</span>301<span>]</span></a></sup> Upon his return to England, he stated: "cannabis is ... less harmful than rum punch, whiskey, nicotine and glue, all of which are perfectly legal ... I don't think ... I was doing anyone any harm whatsoever."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHarry2002306_349-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHarry2002306-349"><span>[</span>302<span>]</span></a></sup> In 1997, he spoke out in support of decriminalisation of the drug: "People are smoking pot anyway and to make them criminals is wrong."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHarry2002307_305-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHarry2002307-305"><span>[</span>258<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Vegetarianism_and_activism">Vegetarianism and activism</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Paul_McCartney_and_Putin_3.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="334" data-file-width="500" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c3/Paul_McCartney_and_Putin_3.jpg/220px-Paul_McCartney_and_Putin_3.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c3/Paul_McCartney_and_Putin_3.jpg/330px-Paul_McCartney_and_Putin_3.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c3/Paul_McCartney_and_Putin_3.jpg/440px-Paul_McCartney_and_Putin_3.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Paul_McCartney_and_Putin_3.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Paul McCartney and Putin in Moskva</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Since 1975, McCartney has been a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Vegetarian" title="Vegetarian">vegetarian</a>; he and his wife Linda were vegetarians for most of their 30-year marriage. They decided to stop consuming meat after Paul saw lambs in a field as they were eating a meal of lamb. Soon after, the couple became outspoken <a href="/wiki/Animal_rights" title="Animal rights">animal rights</a> activists.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHarry2002880.E2.80.93882_350-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHarry2002880.E2.80.93882-350"><span>[</span>303<span>]</span></a></sup> In his first interview after Linda's death, he promised to continue working for animal rights, and in 1999 he spent £3,000,000 to ensure <a href="/wiki/Linda_McCartney_Foods" title="Linda McCartney Foods">Linda McCartney Foods</a> remained free of <a href="/wiki/Genetic_engineering" title="Genetic engineering">genetically engineered</a> ingredients.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-351"><a href="#cite_note-351"><span>[</span>304<span>]</span></a></sup> In 1995, he narrated the documentary <i><a href="/wiki/Devour_the_Earth" title="Devour the Earth">Devour the Earth</a></i>, written by <a href="/wiki/Tony_Wardle" title="Tony Wardle">Tony Wardle</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-352"><a href="#cite_note-352"><span>[</span>305<span>]</span></a></sup> McCartney is a supporter of the animal-rights organisation <a href="/wiki/People_for_the_Ethical_Treatment_of_Animals" title="People for the Ethical Treatment of Animals">People for the Ethical Treatment of Animals</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-353"><a href="#cite_note-353"><span>[</span>306<span>]</span></a></sup> He has appeared in the group's campaigns and, in 2009, he narrated a short <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Factory_farm" title="Factory farm">factory farm</a> exposé titled "Glass Walls."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-354"><a href="#cite_note-354"><span>[</span>307<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-355"><a href="#cite_note-355"><span>[</span>308<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-356"><a href="#cite_note-356"><span>[</span>309<span>]</span></a></sup> McCartney has also supported campaigns headed by the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Humane_Society_of_the_United_States" title="Humane Society of the United States">Humane Society of the United States</a>, <a href="/wiki/Humane_Society_International" title="Humane Society International">Humane Society International</a>, <a href="/wiki/World_Animal_Protection" title="World Animal Protection">World Animal Protection</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/David_Shepherd_(artist)" title="David Shepherd (artist)">David Shepherd Wildlife Foundation</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-357"><a href="#cite_note-357"><span>[</span>310<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-358"><a href="#cite_note-358"><span>[</span>311<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-359"><a href="#cite_note-359"><span>[</span>312<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Following McCartney's marriage to Mills, he joined her in a campaign against <a href="/wiki/Land_mine" title="Land mine">land mines</a>, becoming a patron of <a href="/wiki/Adopt-A-Minefield" title="Adopt-A-Minefield">Adopt-A-Minefield</a>. He wore an anti-landmines T-shirt during some of the Back in the World tour shows.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-360"><a href="#cite_note-360"><span>[</span>313<span>]</span></a></sup> In 2006, the McCartneys travelled to <a href="/wiki/Prince_Edward_Island" title="Prince Edward Island">Prince Edward Island</a> to raise international awareness of <a href="/wiki/Seal_hunting" title="Seal hunting">seal hunting</a>. The couple debated with <a href="/wiki/Danny_Williams_(politician)" title="Danny Williams (politician)">Danny Williams</a>, Newfoundland's then Premier, on <i><a href="/wiki/Larry_King_Live" title="Larry King Live">Larry King Live</a></i>, stating that fishermen should stop hunting seals and start seal-watching businesses instead.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-361"><a href="#cite_note-361"><span>[</span>314<span>]</span></a></sup> McCartney also supports the <a href="/wiki/Make_Poverty_History" title="Make Poverty History">Make Poverty History</a> campaign.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-362"><a href="#cite_note-362"><span>[</span>315<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>McCartney has participated in several charity recordings and performances, including the <a href="/wiki/Concerts_for_the_People_of_Kampuchea" title="Concerts for the People of Kampuchea">Concerts for the People of Kampuchea</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ferry_Aid" title="Ferry Aid">Ferry Aid</a>, <a href="/wiki/Band_Aid_(band)" title="Band Aid (band)">Band Aid</a>, <a href="/wiki/Live_Aid" title="Live Aid">Live Aid</a>, <a href="/wiki/Live_8" title="Live 8">Live 8</a>, and the recording of "<a href="/wiki/Ferry_Cross_the_Mersey" title="Ferry Cross the Mersey">Ferry Cross the Mersey</a>".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-363"><a href="#cite_note-363"><span>[</span>316<span>]</span></a></sup> In 2004, he donated a song to an album to aid the "US Campaign for Burma", in support of Burmese Nobel Prize winner <a href="/wiki/Aung_San_Suu_Kyi" title="Aung San Suu Kyi">Aung San Suu Kyi</a>. In 2008, he donated a song to <a href="/wiki/Aid_Still_Required" title="Aid Still Required">Aid Still Required's</a> CD, organised as an effort to raise funds to assist with the recovery from the devastation caused in Southeast Asia by the 2004 tsunami.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-364"><a href="#cite_note-364"><span>[</span>317<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>In 2009, McCartney wrote to <a href="/wiki/14th_Dalai_Lama" title="14th Dalai Lama">Tenzin Gyatso</a>, the 14th <a href="/wiki/Dalai_Lama" title="Dalai Lama">Dalai Lama</a>, asking him why he was not a vegetarian. As McCartney explained, "He wrote back very kindly, saying, 'my doctors tell me that I must eat meat'. And I wrote back again, saying, you know, I don't think that's right ... I think he's now being told ... that he can get his protein somewhere else ... It just doesn't seem right – the Dalai Lama, on the one hand, saying, 'Hey guys, don't harm sentient beings ... Oh, and by the way, I'm having a steak.'"<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-365"><a href="#cite_note-365"><span>[</span>318<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Save_the_Arctic" title="Save the Arctic">Save the Arctic</a> is a campaign to protect the Arctic and an international outcry and a renewed focus concern on <a href="/wiki/Petroleum_exploration_in_the_Arctic" title="Petroleum exploration in the Arctic">oil development</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Arctic" title="Arctic">Arctic</a>, attracting the support of more than five million people. This includes McCartney, Archbishop <a href="/wiki/Desmond_Tutu" title="Desmond Tutu">Desmond Tutu</a> and 11 <a href="/wiki/Nobel_Peace_Prize" title="Nobel Peace Prize">Nobel Peace Prize</a> winners.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-366"><a href="#cite_note-366"><span>[</span>319<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-367"><a href="#cite_note-367"><span>[</span>320<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>In 2014, McCartney narrated a video for <a href="/wiki/People_for_the_Ethical_Treatment_of_Animals" title="People for the Ethical Treatment of Animals">People for the Ethical Treatment of Animals</a>, titled "Glass Walls", which was harshly critical of <a href="/wiki/Slaughterhouse" title="Slaughterhouse">slaughterhouses</a>, the meat industry, and their effect on <a href="/wiki/Animal_welfare" title="Animal welfare">animal welfare</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-368"><a href="#cite_note-368"><span>[</span>321<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Meditation">Meditation</span></h3>
<p>In August 1967, McCartney met the <a href="/wiki/Maharishi_Mahesh_Yogi" title="Maharishi Mahesh Yogi">Maharishi Mahesh Yogi</a> at the <a href="/wiki/London_Hilton_Hotel" title="London Hilton Hotel">London Hilton</a> and later went to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bangor,_Wales" title="Bangor, Wales">Bangor</a> in North Wales to attend a weekend initiation conference, where he and the other Beatles learned the basics of <a href="/wiki/Transcendental_Meditation" title="Transcendental Meditation">Transcendental Meditation</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELewisohn1992261_369-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELewisohn1992261-369"><span>[</span>322<span>]</span></a></sup> He said, "The whole meditation experience was very good and I still use the mantra ... I find it soothing."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMiles1997396_370-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMiles1997396-370"><span>[</span>323<span>]</span></a></sup> In 2009, McCartney and Starr headlined a benefit concert at <a href="/wiki/Radio_City_Music_Hall" title="Radio City Music Hall">Radio City Music Hall</a>, raising three million dollars for the <a href="/wiki/David_Lynch_Foundation" title="David Lynch Foundation">David Lynch Foundation</a> to fund instruction in Transcendental Meditation for at-risk youth.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-371"><a href="#cite_note-371"><span>[</span>324<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Football">Football</span></h3>
