<p>McCartney has publicly professed support for <a href="/wiki/Everton_F.C." title="Everton F.C.">Everton</a>, and also shown favour for <a href="/wiki/Liverpool_F.C." title="Liverpool F.C.">Liverpool</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-372"><a href="#cite_note-372"><span>[</span>325<span>]</span></a></sup> In 2008, he ended speculation about his allegiance when he said, "Here's the deal: my father was born in Everton, my family are officially Evertonians, so if it comes down to a derby match or an FA Cup final between the two, I would have to support Everton. But after a concert at Wembley Arena I got a bit of a friendship with <a href="/wiki/Kenny_Dalglish" title="Kenny Dalglish">Kenny Dalglish</a>, who had been to the gig and I thought 'You know what? I am just going to support them both because it's all Liverpool.'"<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-373"><a href="#cite_note-373"><span>[</span>326<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Personal_relationships">Personal relationships</span></h2>
<div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Personal_relationships_of_Paul_McCartney" title="Personal relationships of Paul McCartney">Personal relationships of Paul McCartney</a></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Girlfriends">Girlfriends</span></h3>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Dot_Rhone">Dot Rhone</span></h4>
<p>McCartney's first serious girlfriend in Liverpool was Dot Rhone, whom he met at the <a href="/wiki/The_Casbah_Coffee_Club" title="The Casbah Coffee Club">Casbah club</a> in 1959.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESpitz2005163_374-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESpitz2005163-374"><span>[</span>327<span>]</span></a></sup> According to Spitz, Rhone felt that McCartney had a compulsion to control situations. He often chose clothes and make-up for her, encouraging her to grow her hair out like <a href="/wiki/Brigitte_Bardot" title="Brigitte Bardot">Brigitte Bardot</a>'s, and at least once insisting she have it re-styled, to disappointing effect.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-375"><a href="#cite_note-375"><span>[</span>328<span>]</span></a></sup> When McCartney first went to Hamburg with the Beatles, he wrote to Rhone regularly, and she accompanied <a href="/wiki/Cynthia_Lennon" title="Cynthia Lennon">Cynthia Lennon</a> to Hamburg when they played there again in 1962.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESpitz2005239.E2.80.93240_376-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESpitz2005239.E2.80.93240-376"><span>[</span>329<span>]</span></a></sup> The couple had a two-and-a-half-year relationship, and were due to marry until Rhone's miscarriage; according to Spitz, McCartney, now "free of obligation", ended the engagement.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESpitz2005348_377-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESpitz2005348-377"><span>[</span>330<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Jane_Asher">Jane Asher</span></h4>
<p>McCartney first met British actress <a href="/wiki/Jane_Asher" title="Jane Asher">Jane Asher</a> on 18 April 1963, when a photographer asked them to pose at a Beatles performance at the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Albert_Hall" title="Royal Albert Hall">Royal Albert Hall</a> in London.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMiles1997101.E2.80.93102_378-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMiles1997101.E2.80.93102-378"><span>[</span>331<span>]</span></a></sup> The two began a relationship, and in November of that year he took up residence with Asher at her parents' home at 57 Wimpole Street, London.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESpitz2005439_379-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESpitz2005439-379"><span>[</span>332<span>]</span></a></sup> They had lived there for more than two years before the couple moved to McCartney's own home in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/St._John%27s_Wood" title="St. John's Wood">St. John's Wood</a>, in March 1966.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-380"><a href="#cite_note-380"><span>[</span>333<span>]</span></a></sup> He wrote several songs while living at the Ashers', including "Yesterday", "<a href="/wiki/And_I_Love_Her" title="And I Love Her">And I Love Her</a>", "<a href="/wiki/You_Won%27t_See_Me" title="You Won't See Me">You Won't See Me</a>" and "<a href="/wiki/I%27m_Looking_Through_You" title="I'm Looking Through You">I'm Looking Through You</a>", the latter three having been inspired by their romance.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMiles1997108_381-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMiles1997108-381"><span>[</span>334<span>]</span></a></sup> They had a five-year relationship and planned to marry, but Asher broke off the engagement after she discovered he had become involved with <a href="/wiki/Francie_Schwartz" title="Francie Schwartz">Francie Schwartz</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-382"><a href="#cite_note-382"><span>[</span>335<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Wives">Wives</span></h3>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Linda_Eastman">Linda Eastman</span></h4>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Paul_McCartney_with_Linda_McCartney_-_Wings_-_1976.jpg"><img alt="McCartney, seated, playing a twelve-string acoustic guitar, Linda McCartney can be seen seated to his right." class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2000" data-file-width="2968" height="148" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5c/Paul_McCartney_with_Linda_McCartney_-_Wings_-_1976.jpg/220px-Paul_McCartney_with_Linda_McCartney_-_Wings_-_1976.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5c/Paul_McCartney_with_Linda_McCartney_-_Wings_-_1976.jpg/330px-Paul_McCartney_with_Linda_McCartney_-_Wings_-_1976.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5c/Paul_McCartney_with_Linda_McCartney_-_Wings_-_1976.jpg/440px-Paul_McCartney_with_Linda_McCartney_-_Wings_-_1976.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Paul_McCartney_with_Linda_McCartney_-_Wings_-_1976.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
McCartney performing with wife Linda in 1976</div>
</div>
</div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Linda_McCartney" title="Linda McCartney">Linda Eastman</a> was a music fan who once commented, "all my teen years were spent with an ear to the radio."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHarry2002585_383-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHarry2002585-383"><span>[</span>336<span>]</span></a></sup> At times, she skipped school to see artists such as <a href="/wiki/Fabian_Forte" title="Fabian Forte">Fabian</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bobby_Darin" title="Bobby Darin">Bobby Darin</a> and <a href="/wiki/Chuck_Berry" title="Chuck Berry">Chuck Berry</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHarry2002585_383-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHarry2002585-383"><span>[</span>336<span>]</span></a></sup> She became a popular photographer with several rock groups, including <a href="/wiki/The_Jimi_Hendrix_Experience" title="The Jimi Hendrix Experience">the Jimi Hendrix Experience</a>, the Grateful Dead, the Doors and the Beatles, whom she first met at Shea Stadium in 1966. She commented, "It was John who interested me at the start. He was my Beatle hero. But when I met him the fascination faded fast, and I found it was Paul I liked."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHarry2002587_384-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHarry2002587-384"><span>[</span>337<span>]</span></a></sup> The pair first properly met in 1967 at a <a href="/wiki/Georgie_Fame" title="Georgie Fame">Georgie Fame</a> concert at <a href="/wiki/The_Bag_O%27Nails" title="The Bag O'Nails">The Bag O'Nails</a> club, during her UK assignment to photograph rock musicians in London. As Paul remembers, "The night Linda and I met, I spotted her across a crowded club, and although I would normally have been nervous chatting her up, I realised I had to ... Pushiness worked for me that night!"<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-385"><a href="#cite_note-385"><span>[</span>338<span>]</span></a></sup> Linda said this about their meeting: "I was quite shameless really. I was with somebody else [that night] ... and I saw Paul at the other side of the room. He looked so beautiful that I made up my mind I would have to pick him up."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHarry2002587_384-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHarry2002587-384"><span>[</span>337<span>]</span></a></sup> The pair married in 1969. About their relationship, Paul said, "We had a lot of fun together ... just the nature of how we are, our favourite thing really is to just hang, to have fun. And Linda's very big on just following the moment."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMiles1997514.E2.80.93515_386-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMiles1997514.E2.80.93515-386"><span>[</span>339<span>]</span></a></sup> He added, "We were crazy. We had a big argument the night before we got married, and it was nearly called off ... [it's] miraculous that we made it. But we did."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMiles1997525_387-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMiles1997525-387"><span>[</span>340<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>The two collaborated musically after the Beatles' break-up, forming Wings in 1971.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHarry2002904.E2.80.93910_388-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHarry2002904.E2.80.93910-388"><span>[</span>341<span>]</span></a></sup> They faced derision from some fans and critics, who questioned her inclusion. She was nervous about performing with Paul, who explained, "she conquered those nerves, got on with it and was really gutsy."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELewisohn200245_389-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELewisohn200245-389"><span>[</span>342<span>]</span></a></sup> Paul defended her musical ability: "I taught Linda the basics of the keyboard ... She took a couple of lessons and learned some bluesy things ... she did very well and made it look easier than it was ... The critics would say, 'She's not really playing' or 'Look at her—she's playing with one finger.' But what they didn't know is that sometimes she was playing a thing called a <a href="/wiki/Minimoog" title="Minimoog">Minimoog</a>, which could only be played with one finger. It was <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Monophonic_synthesizer" title="Monophonic synthesizer">monophonic</a>."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELewisohn200245_389-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELewisohn200245-389"><span>[</span>342<span>]</span></a></sup> He went on to say, "We thought we were in it for the fun ... it was just something we wanted to do, so if we got it wrong – big deal. We didn't have to justify ourselves."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELewisohn200245_389-2"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELewisohn200245-389"><span>[</span>342<span>]</span></a></sup> Former Wings guitarist McCullough said of collaborating with Linda, "trying to get things together with a learner in the group didn't work as far as I was concerned."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBlaney200784_390-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBlaney200784-390"><span>[</span>343<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>They had four children—Linda's daughter <a href="/wiki/Heather_McCartney" title="Heather McCartney">Heather</a> (legally adopted by Paul), <a href="/wiki/Mary_McCartney" title="Mary McCartney">Mary</a>, <a href="/wiki/Stella_McCartney" title="Stella McCartney">Stella</a> and <a href="/wiki/James_McCartney" title="James McCartney">James</a>—and remained married until Linda's death from breast cancer at age 56 in 1998.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHarry2002585.E2.80.93601_391-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHarry2002585.E2.80.93601-391"><span>[</span>344<span>]</span></a></sup> After her death, Paul stated in <i><a href="/wiki/Daily_Mail" title="Daily Mail">The Daily Mail</a></i>, "I got a counsellor because I knew that I would need some help. He was great, particularly in helping me get rid of my guilt [about wishing I'd been] perfect all the time ... a real bugger. But then I thought, hang on a minute. We're just human. That was the beautiful thing about our marriage. We were just a boyfriend and girlfriend having babies."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHarry2002600.E2.80.93601_392-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHarry2002600.E2.80.93601-392"><span>[</span>345<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Heather_Mills">Heather Mills</span></h4>
<p>In 2002, McCartney married <a href="/wiki/Heather_Mills" title="Heather Mills">Heather Mills</a>, a former model and anti-<a href="/wiki/Land_mine" title="Land mine">landmines</a> campaigner.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHarry2002568.E2.80.93578_393-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHarry2002568.E2.80.93578-393"><span>[</span>346<span>]</span></a></sup> In 2003, the couple had a child, Beatrice Milly, named in honour of Mills' late mother, and one of McCartney's aunts.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESounes2010523_211-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESounes2010523-211"><span>[</span>172<span>]</span></a></sup> They separated in April 2006 and divorced acrimoniously in March 2008.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-394"><a href="#cite_note-394"><span>[</span>347<span>]</span></a></sup> In 2004, he commented on media animosity toward his partners: "[the British public] didn't like me giving up on Jane Asher ... I married [Linda], a New York divorcee with a child, and at the time they didn't like that".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MaccaSMH_395-0"><a href="#cite_note-MaccaSMH-395"><span>[</span>348<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Nancy_Shevell">Nancy Shevell</span></h4>
<p>McCartney married New Yorker Nancy Shevell in a civil ceremony at Old Marylebone Town Hall, London, on 9 October 2011. The wedding was a modest event attended by a group of about 30 relatives and friends.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BBC_News_237-1"><a href="#cite_note-BBC_News-237"><span>[</span>191<span>]</span></a></sup> The couple had been dating since November 2007.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-396"><a href="#cite_note-396"><span>[</span>349<span>]</span></a></sup> Shevell is vice-president of a family-owned transportation conglomerate which owns <a href="/wiki/New_England_Motor_Freight" title="New England Motor Freight">New England Motor Freight</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-397"><a href="#cite_note-397"><span>[</span>350<span>]</span></a></sup> She is a former member of the board of the <a href="/wiki/Metropolitan_Transportation_Authority_(New_York)" title="Metropolitan Transportation Authority (New York)">New York Metropolitan Transportation Authority</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-398"><a href="#cite_note-398"><span>[</span>351<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Beatles">Beatles</span></h3>
<div class="hatnote">This section is about social and other general interactions.  For creative collaborations, see <a href="/wiki/Collaborations_between_ex-Beatles" title="Collaborations between ex-Beatles">Collaborations between ex-Beatles</a>.</div>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="John_Lennon">John Lennon</span></h4>
<p>Though McCartney had a strained relationship with Lennon, they briefly became close again in early 1974, and <a href="/wiki/A_Toot_and_a_Snore_in_%2774" title="A Toot and a Snore in '74">played music together</a> on one occasion.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-399"><a href="#cite_note-399"><span>[</span>352<span>]</span></a></sup> In later years, the two grew apart.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMiles1997587_400-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMiles1997587-400"><span>[</span>353<span>]</span></a></sup> While McCartney would often phone Lennon, he was apprehensive about the reception he would receive. During one call, Lennon told him, "You're all pizza and fairytales!"<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMiles1997588_401-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMiles1997588-401"><span>[</span>354<span>]</span></a></sup> In an effort to avoid talking only about business, they often spoke of cats, babies or baking bread.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMiles1997590_402-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMiles1997590-402"><span>[</span>355<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>On 24 April 1976, the two were watching an episode of <i><a href="/wiki/Saturday_Night_Live" title="Saturday Night Live">Saturday Night Live</a></i> together at Lennon's home in <a href="/wiki/The_Dakota" title="The Dakota">The Dakota</a>, during which <a href="/wiki/Lorne_Michaels" title="Lorne Michaels">Lorne Michaels</a> made a $3,000 cash offer for the Beatles to reunite. While they seriously considered going to the <i>SNL</i> studio a few blocks away, they decided it was too late. This was their last time together.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-403"><a href="#cite_note-403"><span>[</span>356<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/VH1" title="VH1">VH1</a> fictionalised this event in the 2000 television film, <i><a href="/wiki/Two_of_Us_(2000_film)" title="Two of Us (2000 film)">Two of Us</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHarry2002869.E2.80.93870_404-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHarry2002869.E2.80.93870-404"><span>[</span>357<span>]</span></a></sup> McCartney's last telephone call to Lennon, days before Lennon and Ono released <i><a href="/wiki/Double_Fantasy" title="Double Fantasy">Double Fantasy</a></i>, was friendly; he said this about the call: "[It is] a consoling factor for me, because I do feel it was sad that we never actually sat down and straightened our differences out. But fortunately for me, the last phone conversation I ever had with him was really great, and we didn't have any kind of blow-up."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-405"><a href="#cite_note-405"><span>[</span>358<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h5><span class="mw-headline" id="Reaction_to_Lennon.27s_murder">Reaction to Lennon's murder</span></h5>
<div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Death_of_John_Lennon" title="Death of John Lennon">Death of John Lennon</a></div>
<div class="quotebox" style="float: right; clear: right; margin: 0.5em 0 0.8em 1.4em; width:20%; padding: 6px; border: 1px solid #aaa; font-size: 88%; background-color: #F9F9F9; padding:8px;">
<div class="" style="position: relative; text-align: left;">
<div>
<p>"John is kinda like a constant ... always there in my being ... in my soul, so I always think of him".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-406"><a href="#cite_note-406"><span>[</span>359<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
</div>
</div>
<div style="text-align: left;">—McCartney, <i>Guitar World</i>, January 2000</div>
</div>
<p>On 9 December 1980, McCartney followed the news that Lennon had been <a href="/wiki/Death_of_John_Lennon" title="Death of John Lennon">murdered</a> the previous night, his death creating a <a href="/wiki/Media_circus" title="Media circus">media frenzy</a> around the surviving members of the band.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECarlin2009255.E2.80.93257_407-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECarlin2009255.E2.80.93257-407"><span>[</span>360<span>]</span></a></sup> That evening, as he was leaving an <a href="/wiki/Oxford_Street" title="Oxford Street">Oxford Street</a> recording studio surrounded by reporters who asked him for his reaction, he responded: "It's a drag". The press quickly criticised him for what appeared to be a superficial response.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHarry2002505_408-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHarry2002505-408"><span>[</span>361<span>]</span></a></sup> He later explained, "When John was killed somebody stuck a microphone at me and said: 'What do you think about it?' I said, 'It's a dra-a-ag' and meant it with every inch of melancholy I could muster. When you put that in print it says, 'McCartney in London today when asked for a comment on his dead friend said, "It's a drag".' It seemed a very flippant comment to make."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHarry2002505_408-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHarry2002505-408"><span>[</span>361<span>]</span></a></sup> He described his first exchange with Ono after the murder, and his last conversation with Lennon:</p>
<blockquote>
<p>I talked to Yoko the day after he was killed, and the first thing she said was, "John was really fond of you." The last telephone conversation I had with him we were still the best of mates. He was always a very warm guy, John. His bluff was all on the surface. He used to take his glasses down, those granny glasses, and say, "it's only me." They were like a wall you know? A shield. Those are the moments I treasure.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHarry2002505_408-2"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHarry2002505-408"><span>[</span>361<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
</blockquote>
<p>In 1983, McCartney said, "I would not have been as typically human and standoffish as I was if I knew John was going to die. I would have made more of an effort to try and get behind his "mask" and have a better relationship with him."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHarry2002505_408-3"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHarry2002505-408"><span>[</span>361<span>]</span></a></sup> He said that he went home that night, watched the news on television with his children and cried most of the evening. In 1997, he admitted the ex-Beatles were nervous at the time that they might also be murdered.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMiles1997594_409-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMiles1997594-409"><span>[</span>362<span>]</span></a></sup> He told <i>Mojo</i> magazine in 2002 that Lennon was his greatest hero.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHarry2002506_410-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHarry2002506-410"><span>[</span>363<span>]</span></a></sup> In 1981, McCartney sang backup on Harrison's tribute to their ex-bandmate, "<a href="/wiki/All_Those_Years_Ago" title="All Those Years Ago">All Those Years Ago</a>", which featured Starr on drums.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHarry200220_411-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHarry200220-411"><span>[</span>364<span>]</span></a></sup> McCartney released "<a href="/wiki/Here_Today_(Paul_McCartney_song)" title="Here Today (Paul McCartney song)">Here Today</a>" in 1982, a song Everett described as "a haunting tribute" to McCartney's friendship with Lennon.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEEverett199910_412-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEEverett199910-412"><span>[</span>365<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="George_Harrison">George Harrison</span></h4>
<p>Discussing his relationship with McCartney, Harrison said, "Paul would always help along when you'd done his ten songs—then when he got 'round to doing one of my songs, he would help. It was silly. It was very selfish, actually ... There were a lot of tracks, though, where I played bass ... because what Paul would do—if he'd written a song, he'd learn all the parts for Paul and then come in the studio and say (sometimes he was very difficult): "Do this". He'd never give you the opportunity to come out with something."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-413"><a href="#cite_note-413"><span>[</span>366<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>After Harrison's death in November 2001, McCartney issued a statement outside his home in St. John's Wood, calling him "a lovely guy and a very brave man who had a wonderful sense of humour". He went on to say, "We grew up together and we just had so many beautiful times together – that's what I am going to remember. I'll always love him, he's my baby brother."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-414"><a href="#cite_note-414"><span>[</span>367<span>]</span></a></sup> On the first anniversary of his death, McCartney played Harrison's "<a href="/wiki/Something_(Beatles_song)" title="Something (Beatles song)">Something</a>" on a <a href="/wiki/Ukulele" title="Ukulele">ukulele</a> at the <a href="/wiki/Concert_for_George" title="Concert for George">Concert for George</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDoggett2009332.E2.80.93333_415-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDoggett2009332.E2.80.93333-415"><span>[</span>368<span>]</span></a></sup> He also performed "<a href="/wiki/For_You_Blue" title="For You Blue">For You Blue</a>" and "<a href="/wiki/All_Things_Must_Pass_(song)" title="All Things Must Pass (song)">All Things Must Pass</a>", and played the piano on <a href="/wiki/Eric_Clapton" title="Eric Clapton">Eric Clapton</a>'s rendition of "<a href="/wiki/While_My_Guitar_Gently_Weeps" title="While My Guitar Gently Weeps">While My Guitar Gently Weeps</a>".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHarry2003138.E2.80.93139_416-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHarry2003138.E2.80.93139-416"><span>[</span>369<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Ringo_Starr">Ringo Starr</span></h4>
<p>Starr once described McCartney as "pleasantly insincere", though the two generally enjoy each other's company, and at least once went on holiday together in Greece.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHarry2002815_417-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHarry2002815-417"><span>[</span>370<span>]</span></a></sup> Starr recalled, "We couldn't understand a word of the songs the hotel band were playing, so on the last night Paul and I did a few rockers like "<a href="/wiki/What%27d_I_Say" title="What'd I Say">What'd I Say</a>".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHarry2002815_417-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHarry2002815-417"><span>[</span>370<span>]</span></a></sup> There was at times discord between them as well, particularly during sessions for <i>the White Album</i>. As Apple's <a href="/wiki/Peter_Brown_(music_industry)" title="Peter Brown (music industry)">Peter Brown</a> recalled, "it was a poorly kept secret among Beatle intimates that after Ringo left the studio Paul would often dub in the drum tracks himself ... [Starr] would pretend not to notice".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBrownGaines2002289_418-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBrownGaines2002289-418"><span>[</span>371<span>]</span></a></sup> In August 1968, the two got into an argument over McCartney's critique of Starr's drum part for "Back in the U.S.S.R.", which contributed to Starr temporarily leaving the band.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-419"><a href="#cite_note-419"><span>[</span>372<span>]</span></a></sup> When Starr returned in September, he found bouquets of flowers on his drum kit.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELewisohn1992296_420-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELewisohn1992296-420"><span>[</span>373<span>]</span></a></sup> Starr commented on working with McCartney: "Paul is the greatest bass player in the world. But he is also very determined ... [to] get his own way ... [thus] musical disagreements inevitably arose from time to time."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHarry2002816_421-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHarry2002816-421"><span>[</span>374<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>McCartney and Starr collaborated on several post-Beatles projects starting in 1973, when McCartney contributed instrumentation and backing vocals for "Six O'Clock", a song McCartney wrote for Starr's album <i><a href="/wiki/Ringo_(album)" title="Ringo (album)">Ringo</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-422"><a href="#cite_note-422"><span>[</span>375<span>]</span></a></sup> McCartney played a <a href="/wiki/Kazoo" title="Kazoo">kazoo</a> solo on another track from the album, "<a href="/wiki/You%27re_Sixteen" title="You're Sixteen">You're Sixteen</a>".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-423"><a href="#cite_note-423"><span>[</span>376<span>]</span></a></sup> Starr appeared (as a fictional version of himself) in McCartney's 1984 film <i><a href="/wiki/Give_My_Regards_to_Broad_Street_(film)" title="Give My Regards to Broad Street (film)">Give My Regards to Broad Street</a></i>, and played drums on most tracks of the <a href="/wiki/Give_My_Regards_to_Broad_Street" title="Give My Regards to Broad Street">soundtrack album</a>, which includes re-recordings of several McCartney-penned Beatles songs. Starr played drums and sang backing vocals on "<a href="/wiki/Beautiful_Night_(Paul_McCartney_song)" title="Beautiful Night (Paul McCartney song)">Beautiful Night</a>" from McCartney's 1997 album, <i>Flaming Pie</i>. The pair collaborated again in 1998, on Starr's <i><a href="/wiki/Vertical_Man" title="Vertical Man">Vertical Man</a></i>, which featured McCartney's backing vocals on three songs, and instrumentation on one.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBlaney2007279.E2.80.93281_424-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBlaney2007279.E2.80.93281-424"><span>[</span>377<span>]</span></a></sup> In 2009, the pair performed "<a href="/wiki/With_a_Little_Help_from_My_Friends" title="With a Little Help from My Friends">With a Little Help from My Friends</a>" at a benefit concert for the <a href="/wiki/David_Lynch_Foundation" title="David Lynch Foundation">David Lynch Foundation</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-425"><a href="#cite_note-425"><span>[</span>378<span>]</span></a></sup> They collaborated on Starr's album, <i><a href="/wiki/Y_Not" title="Y Not">Y Not</a></i>, in 2010. McCartney played bass on "Peace Dream", and sang a <a href="/wiki/Duet" title="Duet">duet</a> with Starr on "<a href="/wiki/Walk_with_You" title="Walk with You">Walk with You</a>".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-426"><a href="#cite_note-426"><span>[</span>379<span>]</span></a></sup> On 7 July 2010, Starr was performing at Radio City Music Hall in New York with his <a href="/wiki/Ringo_Starr_%26_His_All-Starr_Band" title="Ringo Starr &amp; His All-Starr Band">All-Starr Band</a> in a concert celebrating his seventieth birthday. After the encores, McCartney made a surprise, last minute appearance, coming out and performing the Beatles' song "<a href="/wiki/Birthday_(Beatles_song)" title="Birthday (Beatles song)">Birthday</a>" backed by members of Starr's band.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-427"><a href="#cite_note-427"><span>[</span>380<span>]</span></a></sup> On 26 January 2014 McCartney and Starr performed "<a href="/wiki/Queenie_Eye" title="Queenie Eye">Queenie Eye</a>" from McCartney's new album <i><a href="/wiki/New_(album)" title="New (album)">New</a></i> at the <a href="/wiki/56th_Annual_Grammy_Awards" title="56th Annual Grammy Awards">56th Annual Grammy Awards</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-428"><a href="#cite_note-428"><span>[</span>381<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Legacy">Legacy</span></h2>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:182px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Paul_McCartney_on_stage_in_Prague.jpg"><img alt="A colour photograph of McCartney, wearing a red coat and blue jeans playing an electric guitar and singing, while performing live on a stage." class="thumbimage" data-file-height="402" data-file-width="278" height="260" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b3/Paul_McCartney_on_stage_in_Prague.jpg/180px-Paul_McCartney_on_stage_in_Prague.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b3/Paul_McCartney_on_stage_in_Prague.jpg/270px-Paul_McCartney_on_stage_in_Prague.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/b/b3/Paul_McCartney_on_stage_in_Prague.jpg 2x" width="180"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Paul_McCartney_on_stage_in_Prague.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
McCartney performing in Prague, June 2004</div>
</div>
</div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Achievements">Achievements</span></h3>
<p>McCartney was inducted into the <a href="/wiki/Rock_and_Roll_Hall_of_Fame" title="Rock and Roll Hall of Fame">Rock and Roll Hall of Fame</a> in 1988 as a member of the Beatles and again as a solo artist in 1999. In 1979, the <i><a href="/wiki/Guinness_World_Records" title="Guinness World Records">Guinness Book of World Records</a></i> recognised McCartney as the "most honored composer and performer in music", with 60 <a href="/wiki/RIAA_certification" title="RIAA certification">gold discs</a> (43 with the Beatles, 17 with Wings) and, as a member of the Beatles, sales of over 100 million singles and 100 million albums, and as the "most successful song writer", he wrote jointly or solo 43 songs which sold one million or more records between 1962 and 1978.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-429"><a href="#cite_note-429"><span>[</span>382<span>]</span></a></sup> In 2009, <i>Guinness World Records</i> again recognised McCartney as the "most successful songwriter" having written or co-written 188 charted records in the United Kingdom, of which 91 reached the top 10 and 33 made it to number one.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-430"><a href="#cite_note-430"><span>[</span>383<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>McCartney has written, or co-written 32 number-one singles on the <i>Billboard</i> Hot 100: twenty with the Beatles; seven solo or with Wings; one as a co-writer of "<a href="/wiki/A_World_Without_Love" title="A World Without Love">A World Without Love</a>", a number-one single for <a href="/wiki/Peter_and_Gordon" title="Peter and Gordon">Peter and Gordon</a>; one as a co-writer on <a href="/wiki/Elton_John" title="Elton John">Elton John</a>'s cover of "Lucy in the Sky with Diamonds"; one as a co-writer on <a href="/wiki/Stars_on_45" title="Stars on 45">Stars on 45</a>'s "Medley"; one as a co-writer with <a href="/wiki/Michael_Jackson" title="Michael Jackson">Michael Jackson</a> on "Say Say Say"; and one as a co-writer with Stevie Wonder on "Ebony and Ivory".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-431"><a href="#cite_note-431"><span>[</span>384<span>]</span></a></sup> As of 2014<sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Paul_McCartney&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, he has sold 15.5 million <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/RIAA" title="RIAA">RIAA</a> certified units in the United States.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-432"><a href="#cite_note-432"><span>[</span>385<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Credited with more number ones in the UK than any other artist, McCartney has participated in twenty-four chart topping singles: seventeen with the Beatles, one solo, and one each with Wings, Stevie Wonder, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Let_It_Be_(Ferry_Aid_song)" title="Let It Be (Ferry Aid song)">Ferry Aid</a>, <a href="/wiki/Band_Aid_(band)" title="Band Aid (band)">Band Aid</a>, <a href="/wiki/Band_Aid_20" title="Band Aid 20">Band Aid 20</a> and "The Christians et al."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-433"><a href="#cite_note-433"><span>[</span>386<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-435"><a href="#cite_note-435"><span>[</span>nb 48<span>]</span></a></sup> He is the only artist to reach the UK number one as a <a href="/wiki/Solo_(music)" title="Solo (music)">soloist</a> ("Pipes of Peace"), duo ("Ebony and Ivory" with Wonder), <a href="/wiki/Trio_(music)" title="Trio (music)">trio</a> ("Mull of Kintyre", Wings), quartet ("She Loves You", the Beatles), quintet ("Get Back", the Beatles with <a href="/wiki/Billy_Preston" title="Billy Preston">Billy Preston</a>) and as part of a musical ensemble for charity (Ferry Aid).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERoberts2005311.E2.80.93312_436-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERoberts2005311.E2.80.93312-436"><span>[</span>388<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>"Yesterday" is the most covered song in history with more than 2,200 recorded versions, and according to the BBC, "the track is the only one by a UK writer to have been aired more than seven million times on American TV and radio and is third in the all-time list ... [and] is the most played song by a British writer [last] century in the US".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-437"><a href="#cite_note-437"><span>[</span>389<span>]</span></a></sup> His 1968 Beatles composition, "Hey Jude", is also a career highlight. It achieved the highest sales in the UK that year, topping the US charts for nine weeks, longer than any other Beatles single. It was also the longest single released by the band, and at seven minutes eleven seconds, the longest ever number one to that point.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBronson1992247_438-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBronson1992247-438"><span>[</span>390<span>]</span></a></sup> "Hey Jude" is the best-selling Beatles single, achieving sales of over five million copies soon after its release.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESounes2010223_439-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESounes2010223-439"><span>[</span>391<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-441"><a href="#cite_note-441"><span>[</span>nb 49<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>In July 2005, McCartney's performance of "Sgt. Pepper's Lonely Hearts Club Band" with <a href="/wiki/U2" title="U2">U2</a> at <a href="/wiki/Live_8" title="Live 8">Live 8</a> became the fastest-released single in history. Available within forty-five minutes of its recording, hours later it had achieved number one on the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/UK_Official_Download_Chart" title="UK Official Download Chart">UK Official Download Chart</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBlaney2007268.E2.80.93269_212-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBlaney2007268.E2.80.93269-212"><span>[</span>173<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Awards">Awards</span></h3>
<div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">Main article: <a href="/wiki/List_of_awards_received_by_Paul_McCartney" title="List of awards received by Paul McCartney">List of awards received by Paul McCartney</a></div>
<p>In <a href="/wiki/1965_Birthday_Honours" title="1965 Birthday Honours">June 1965</a>, McCartney, Lennon, Harrison and Starr, were made <a href="/wiki/Order_of_the_British_Empire" title="Order of the British Empire">Members of the Order of the British Empire</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELondon_Gazette19655487.E2.80.935489_442-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELondon_Gazette19655487.E2.80.935489-442"><span>[</span>393<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESpitz2005556_443-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESpitz2005556-443"><span>[</span>394<span>]</span></a></sup> In 1990, the <a href="/wiki/International_Astronomical_Union" title="International Astronomical Union">IAU</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Minor_Planet_Center" title="Minor Planet Center">Minor Planet Center</a> named the planet <a href="/wiki/4148_McCartney" title="4148 McCartney">4148</a>, "McCartney" in his honour.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-444"><a href="#cite_note-444"><span>[</span>395<span>]</span></a></sup> In March 1997, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Queen_Elizabeth_II" title="Queen Elizabeth II">Queen Elizabeth II</a> <a href="/wiki/Knight_Bachelor" title="Knight Bachelor">knighted</a> him for services to music.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHarry2002226.E2.80.93227_445-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHarry2002226.E2.80.93227-445"><span>[</span>396<span>]</span></a></sup> In May 2000, the <a href="/wiki/British_Academy_of_Songwriters,_Composers_and_Authors" title="British Academy of Songwriters, Composers and Authors">British Academy of Songwriters, Composers and Authors</a> awarded him a Fellowship.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHarry200238.2C_242_446-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHarry200238.2C_242-446"><span>[</span>397<span>]</span></a></sup> In 2008, he received a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/BRIT_Award" title="BRIT Award">BRIT Award</a> for Outstanding Contribution to Music, as well as an honorary <a href="/wiki/Doctor_of_Music" title="Doctor of Music">Doctor of Music</a> degree from <a href="/wiki/Yale_University" title="Yale University">Yale University</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-447"><a href="#cite_note-447"><span>[</span>398<span>]</span></a></sup> In 2010, President <a href="/wiki/Barack_Obama" title="Barack Obama">Barack Obama</a> honoured McCartney with the <a href="/wiki/Gershwin_Prize" title="Gershwin Prize">Gershwin Prize</a> for his contributions to popular music.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-448"><a href="#cite_note-448"><span>[</span>399<span>]</span></a></sup> He returned to the White House later that year as a recipient of the <a href="/wiki/Kennedy_Center_Honors" title="Kennedy Center Honors">Kennedy Center Honors</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-449"><a href="#cite_note-449"><span>[</span>400<span>]</span></a></sup> McCartney won two Grammy awards with Wings, and two as a solo artist.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-450"><a href="#cite_note-450"><span>[</span>401<span>]</span></a></sup> In 2012, he became the last Beatle to receive a star on the <a href="/wiki/Hollywood_Walk_of_Fame" title="Hollywood Walk of Fame">Hollywood Walk of Fame</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-451"><a href="#cite_note-451"><span>[</span>402<span>]</span></a></sup> On 8 September 2012, during a ceremony in Paris, French President <a href="/wiki/Fran%C3%A7ois_Hollande" title="François Hollande">François Hollande</a> decorated McCartney with the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/L%C3%A9gion_d%27Honneur" title="Légion d'Honneur">Légion d'Honneur</a>, with a rank of officer, for his services to music.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-452"><a href="#cite_note-452"><span>[</span>403<span>]</span></a></sup></p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Notes">Notes</span></h2>
<div class="reflist references-column-width" style="-moz-column-width: 30em; -webkit-column-width: 30em; column-width: 30em; list-style-type: decimal;">
<ol class="references">
<li id="cite_note-15"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-15">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Jim McCartney's father Joe played an E-flat <a href="/wiki/Tuba" title="Tuba">tuba</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESpitz200571_13-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESpitz200571-13"><span>[</span>13<span>]</span></a></sup> He pointed out the bass parts in songs on the radio, and often took his sons to local <a href="/wiki/Brass_band" title="Brass band">brass band</a> concerts.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMiles199723.E2.80.9324_14-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMiles199723.E2.80.9324-14"><span>[</span>14<span>]</span></a></sup></span></li>
<li id="cite_note-26"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-26">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">During their extended stays there over the next two years, they performed as the resident group at the Indra, and later the <a href="/wiki/Kaiserkeller" title="Kaiserkeller">Kaiserkeller</a>, both owned by <a href="/wiki/Bruno_Koschmider" title="Bruno Koschmider">Bruno Koschmider</a>. Periodically, the band received breaks from playing in Hamburg and returned to Liverpool, performing regularly at <a href="/wiki/The_Cavern_Club" title="The Cavern Club">the Cavern Club</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-25"><a href="#cite_note-25"><span>[</span>24<span>]</span></a></sup></span></li>
<li id="cite_note-32"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-32">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">In 1963, the Beatles released two studio albums: <i><a href="/wiki/Please_Please_Me" title="Please Please Me">Please Please Me</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/With_the_Beatles" title="With the Beatles">With the Beatles</a></i>. Two more albums followed in 1964: <i><a href="/wiki/A_Hard_Day%27s_Night_(album)" title="A Hard Day's Night (album)">A Hard Day's Night</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Beatles_for_Sale" title="Beatles for Sale">Beatles for Sale</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELewisohn1992350.E2.80.93351_31-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELewisohn1992350.E2.80.93351-31"><span>[</span>29<span>]</span></a></sup></span></li>
<li id="cite_note-34"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-34">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">McCartney co-wrote (with Lennon) several of their early hits, including "<a href="/wiki/I_Saw_Her_Standing_There" title="I Saw Her Standing There">I Saw Her Standing There</a>", "<a href="/wiki/She_Loves_You" title="She Loves You">She Loves You</a>", "<a href="/wiki/I_Want_to_Hold_Your_Hand" title="I Want to Hold Your Hand">I Want to Hold Your Hand</a>" (1963) and "<a href="/wiki/Can%27t_Buy_Me_Love" title="Can't Buy Me Love">Can't Buy Me Love</a>" (1964).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33"><a href="#cite_note-33"><span>[</span>30<span>]</span></a></sup></span></li>
<li id="cite_note-48"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-48">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Also included on <i>Revolver</i> was "<a href="/wiki/Here,_There_and_Everywhere" title="Here, There and Everywhere">Here, There and Everywhere</a>", a McCartney composition which is his second favourite after "Yesterday".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEEverett1999328_47-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEEverett1999328-47"><span>[</span>43<span>]</span></a></sup></span></li>
<li id="cite_note-59"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-59">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Written by McCartney as a commentary on his childhood in Liverpool, "Penny Lane" featured a <a href="/wiki/Piccolo_trumpet" title="Piccolo trumpet">piccolo trumpet</a> solo inspired by <a href="/wiki/Johann_Sebastian_Bach" title="Johann Sebastian Bach">Bach</a>'s second <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Brandenburg_concertos" title="Brandenburg concertos">Brandenburg concerto</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESounes2010161.E2.80.93162_58-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESounes2010161.E2.80.93162-58"><span>[</span>53<span>]</span></a></sup></span></li>
<li id="cite_note-63"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-63">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">The <i>Sgt. Pepper</i> cover piqued a frenzy of analysis.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-62"><a href="#cite_note-62"><span>[</span>56<span>]</span></a></sup></span></li>
<li id="cite_note-75"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-75">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><i>The Beatles</i> was the band's first <a href="/wiki/Apple_Records" title="Apple Records">Apple Records</a> LP release; the label was a subsidiary of <a href="/wiki/Apple_Corps" title="Apple Corps">Apple Corps</a>, a conglomerate formed as part of Epstein's plan to reduce the group's taxes.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-74"><a href="#cite_note-74"><span>[</span>67<span>]</span></a></sup></span></li>
<li id="cite_note-80"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-80">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">In October 1969, <a href="/wiki/Paul_is_dead" title="Paul is dead">a rumour surfaced</a> that McCartney had died in a car crash in 1966 and been replaced by a lookalike, but this was quickly refuted when a November <i><a href="/wiki/Life_(magazine)" title="Life (magazine)">Life</a></i> magazine cover featured him and his family, accompanied by the caption "Paul is still with us".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGould2007593.E2.80.93594_79-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGould2007593.E2.80.93594-79"><span>[</span>71<span>]</span></a></sup></span></li>
<li id="cite_note-83"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-83">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">When the Beatles were inducted into the <a href="/wiki/Rock_and_Roll_Hall_of_Fame" title="Rock and Roll Hall of Fame">Rock and Roll Hall of Fame</a> in 1988, their first year of eligibility, McCartney did not attend the ceremony, stating that unresolved legal disputes would make him "feel like a complete hypocrite waving and smiling with [Harrison and Starr] at a fake reunion."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHarry2002753_82-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHarry2002753-82"><span>[</span>73<span>]</span></a></sup></span></li>
<li id="cite_note-87"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-87">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">The Beatles released twenty-two UK singles and twelve LPs, of which seventeen singles and eleven LPs reached number one on various charts.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERoberts200554_84-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERoberts200554-84"><span>[</span>74<span>]</span></a></sup> The band topped the US <a href="/wiki/Billboard_Hot_100" title="Billboard Hot 100"><i>Billboard</i> Hot 100</a> twenty times, and recorded fourteen number-one albums, as Lennon and McCartney became one of the most celebrated <a href="/wiki/Lennon%E2%80%93McCartney" title="Lennon–McCartney">songwriting partnerships</a> of the 20th century.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-85"><a href="#cite_note-85"><span>[</span>75<span>]</span></a></sup> McCartney was the primary writer of five of their last six US number-one singles: "<a href="/wiki/Hello,_Goodbye" title="Hello, Goodbye">Hello, Goodbye</a>" (1967), "<a href="/wiki/Hey_Jude" title="Hey Jude">Hey Jude</a>" (1968), "<a href="/wiki/Get_Back" title="Get Back">Get Back</a> (1969)", "<a href="/wiki/Let_It_Be_(song)" title="Let It Be (song)">Let It Be</a>" and "<a href="/wiki/The_Long_and_Winding_Road" title="The Long and Winding Road">The Long and Winding Road</a>" (1970).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-86"><a href="#cite_note-86"><span>[</span>76<span>]</span></a></sup></span></li>
<li id="cite_note-92"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-92">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><i>McCartney</i> peaked in the UK at number two, spending thirty-two weeks in the charts.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-91"><a href="#cite_note-91"><span>[</span>80<span>]</span></a></sup></span></li>
<li id="cite_note-96"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-96">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Wings' first album together, <i><a href="/wiki/Wild_Life_(Wings_album)" title="Wild Life (Wings album)">Wild Life</a></i>, reached the top ten in the US and the top twenty in the UK, staying on the UK charts for nine weeks.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-95"><a href="#cite_note-95"><span>[</span>83<span>]</span></a></sup></span></li>
<li id="cite_note-102"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-102">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">In May 1973, Wings began a <a href="/wiki/Wings_1973_UK_Tour" title="Wings 1973 UK Tour">21-show tour of the UK</a>, this time with supporting act <a href="/wiki/Brinsley_Schwarz" title="Brinsley Schwarz">Brinsley Schwarz</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHarry2002847_100-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHarry2002847-100"><span>[</span>87<span>]</span></a></sup></span></li>
<li id="cite_note-106"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-106">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">"Live and Let Die" became a staple of McCartney's live shows, its modern sound well-suited for the <a href="/wiki/Pyrotechnics" title="Pyrotechnics">pyrotechnics</a> and <a href="/wiki/Laser_lighting_display" title="Laser lighting display">laser light displays</a> Wings employed during their 1970s stadium performances.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-105"><a href="#cite_note-105"><span>[</span>91<span>]</span></a></sup></span></li>
<li id="cite_note-110"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-110">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><i>Band on the Run</i> became the UK's first <a href="/wiki/Music_recording_sales_certification" title="Music recording sales certification">platinum LP</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMcGee200360_109-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMcGee200360-109"><span>[</span>94<span>]</span></a></sup></span></li>
<li id="cite_note-114"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-114">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">In 1974, McCartney hired guitarist <a href="/wiki/Jimmy_McCulloch" title="Jimmy McCulloch">Jimmy McCulloch</a> and drummer <a href="/wiki/Geoff_Britton" title="Geoff Britton">Geoff Britton</a> to replace McCullough and Seiwell. Britton subsequently quit during recording sessions in 1975 and was replaced by <a href="/wiki/Joe_English_(musician)" title="Joe English (musician)">Joe English</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBenitez201061.E2.80.9362_113-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBenitez201061.E2.80.9362-113"><span>[</span>97<span>]</span></a></sup></span></li>
<li id="cite_note-117"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-117">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><i>Wings at the Speed of Sound</i> peaked in the UK at number 2, spending 35 weeks in the charts. In the UK, <i>NME</i> was alone in ranking the album number 1. The LP reached number 1 on three charts in the US.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-116"><a href="#cite_note-116"><span>[</span>99<span>]</span></a></sup></span></li>
<li id="cite_note-123"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-123">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">In 1977, McCartney released the album <i><a href="/wiki/Thrillington" title="Thrillington">Thrillington</a></i>, an orchestral arrangement of <i>Ram</i>, under the pseudonym Percy "Thrills" Thrillington, with a cover designed by <a href="/wiki/Hipgnosis" title="Hipgnosis">Hipgnosis</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-122"><a href="#cite_note-122"><span>[</span>104<span>]</span></a></sup></span></li>
<li id="cite_note-126"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-126">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">During the production of <i>London Town</i>, McCulloch and English quit Wings; they were replaced by guitarist <a href="/wiki/Laurence_Juber" title="Laurence Juber">Laurence Juber</a> and drummer Steve Holly.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBenitez201079_125-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBenitez201079-125"><span>[</span>106<span>]</span></a></sup></span></li>
<li id="cite_note-133"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-133">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Other factors in Wings' split included tension caused by the disappointment of their last effort, <i>Back to the Egg</i>, and McCartney's 1980 <a href="/wiki/Cannabis_(drug)" title="Cannabis (drug)">marijuana</a> bust in Japan, which resulted in the cancelling of the tour and caused a major loss of wages for the group. Laine claimed that a significant cause of their dissolution was McCartney's reluctance to tour, fearing for his personal safety after the <a href="/wiki/Death_of_John_Lennon" title="Death of John Lennon">1980 murder of Lennon</a>. McCartney's then-spokesman said, "Paul is doing other things, that's all".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-132"><a href="#cite_note-132"><span>[</span>112<span>]</span></a></sup></span></li>
<li id="cite_note-136"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-136">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Wings produced a total of seven studio albums, two of which topped the UK charts and four the US charts. Their live triple LP, <i>Wings over America</i>, was one of only a few live albums ever to achieve the top spot in America.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-134"><a href="#cite_note-134"><span>[</span>113<span>]</span></a></sup> They made six US <i>Billboard</i> number-one singles, including "<a href="/wiki/Listen_to_What_the_Man_Said" title="Listen to What the Man Said">Listen to What the Man Said</a>" and "<a href="/wiki/Silly_Love_Songs" title="Silly Love Songs">Silly Love Songs</a>", as well as eight top-ten singles. They achieved eight RIAA-certified platinum singles and six platinum albums in the US.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMcGee2003248.E2.80.93249_107-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMcGee2003248.E2.80.93249-107"><span>[</span>92<span>]</span></a></sup> In the UK, they achieved one number-one and twelve top-ten singles, as well as two number-one LPs.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-135"><a href="#cite_note-135"><span>[</span>114<span>]</span></a></sup></span></li>
<li id="cite_note-139"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-139">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><i>Tug of War</i> was a number-one album in both the UK and the US.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBlaney2007153_138-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBlaney2007153-138"><span>[</span>116<span>]</span></a></sup></span></li>
<li id="cite_note-143"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-143">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><i>Pipes of Peace</i> peaked in the UK at number 4, spending 23 weeks in the charts. The LP reached number 15 in the US and is McCartney's most recently recorded <a href="/wiki/Recording_Industry_Association_of_America" title="Recording Industry Association of America">RIAA</a> certified platinum studio album as of 2012<sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Paul_McCartney&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-142"><a href="#cite_note-142"><span>[</span>119<span>]</span></a></sup></span></li>
<li id="cite_note-149"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-149">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">"Spies Like Us" peaked in the UK at number 13 spending 10 weeks in the charts. The single reached number 7 in the US and is McCartney's most recently recorded US top-ten as of 2012.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-148"><a href="#cite_note-148"><span>[</span>124<span>]</span></a></sup></span></li>
<li id="cite_note-153"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-153">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><i>Press to Play</i> reached number 8 in the UK, and number 30 in the US.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-152"><a href="#cite_note-152"><span>[</span>127<span>]</span></a></sup></span></li>
<li id="cite_note-157"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-157">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">In 1989, "Ferry Cross the Mersey" reached number 1 in the UK.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERoberts2005688.E2.80.93689_156-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERoberts2005688.E2.80.93689-156"><span>[</span>130<span>]</span></a></sup></span></li>
<li id="cite_note-160"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-160">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><i>Flowers in the Dirt</i> is McCartney's most recent UK number-one album as of 2012; it reached number 21 in the US.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-159"><a href="#cite_note-159"><span>[</span>132<span>]</span></a></sup></span></li>
<li id="cite_note-164"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-164">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><i>Tripping the Live Fantastic</i> reached number 17 in the UK and number 26 in the US.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBlaney2007201_163-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBlaney2007201-163"><span>[</span>135<span>]</span></a></sup></span></li>
<li id="cite_note-166"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-166">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">During the ten-month, 104-show <i>Tripping the Live Fantastic</i> tour, McCartney played as many as fourteen Beatles songs a night, comprising nearly half the performance.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESounes2010512_165-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESounes2010512-165"><span>[</span>136<span>]</span></a></sup></span></li>
<li id="cite_note-175"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-175">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><i>Unplugged: The Official Bootleg</i> reached number 7 in the UK and number 14 in the US.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBlaney2007205_174-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBlaney2007205-174"><span>[</span>144<span>]</span></a></sup></span></li>
<li id="cite_note-179"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-179">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><i>Off the Ground</i> reached number 5 in the UK and number 17 in the US.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBlaney2007215_178-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBlaney2007215-178"><span>[</span>147<span>]</span></a></sup></span></li>
<li id="cite_note-182"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-182">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><i>Paul is Live</i> reached number 34 in the UK and number 78 in the US.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBlaney2007219_181-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBlaney2007219-181"><span>[</span>149<span>]</span></a></sup></span></li>
<li id="cite_note-185"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-185">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">For the New World Tour, Whitten was replaced by drummer <a href="/wiki/Blair_Cunningham" title="Blair Cunningham">Blair Cunningham</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESounes2010429_183-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESounes2010429-183"><span>[</span>150<span>]</span></a></sup> McCartney's 1993 tour of the US was the second highest grossing effort of the year in America, bringing in $32.3 million from twenty-four shows.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEEverett1999282_184-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEEverett1999282-184"><span>[</span>151<span>]</span></a></sup></span></li>
<li id="cite_note-190"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-190">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><i>Flaming Pie</i> reached number 2 in the UK and the US. It also yielded McCartney's highest charting UK top-twenty hit song as of 2012<sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Paul_McCartney&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, "<a href="/wiki/Young_Boy" title="Young Boy">Young Boy</a>", which reached number 19.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-189"><a href="#cite_note-189"><span>[</span>155<span>]</span></a></sup></span></li>
<li id="cite_note-194"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-194">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><i>Run Devil Run</i> reached number 12 in the UK and number 27 in the US.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBlaney2007241_193-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBlaney2007241-193"><span>[</span>158<span>]</span></a></sup></span></li>
<li id="cite_note-201"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-201">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><i>Driving Rain</i> reached number 46 in the UK and number 26 in the US.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBlaney2007255_200-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBlaney2007255-200"><span>[</span>164<span>]</span></a></sup></span></li>
<li id="cite_note-205"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-205">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><i>Back in the US</i> reached number 8 in the US, and <i>Back in the World</i> reached number 5 in the UK.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-204"><a href="#cite_note-204"><span>[</span>167<span>]</span></a></sup></span></li>
<li id="cite_note-206"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-206">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">During the Driving World Tour McCartney performed twenty-three Beatles songs in a thirty-six song set, including an all-Beatles encore.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESounes2010512_165-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESounes2010512-165"><span>[</span>136<span>]</span></a></sup></span></li>
<li id="cite_note-214"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-214">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">In June 2005, McCartney released the electronica album <i><a href="/wiki/Twin_Freaks" title="Twin Freaks">Twin Freaks</a></i>, a collaborative project with <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bastard_pop" title="Bastard pop">bootleg</a> producer and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Remixer" title="Remixer">remixer</a> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Freelance_Hellraiser" title="Freelance Hellraiser">Freelance Hellraiser</a> consisting of remixed versions of songs from his solo career.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBlaney2007268_213-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBlaney2007268-213"><span>[</span>174<span>]</span></a></sup></span></li>
<li id="cite_note-217"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-217">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><i>Chaos and Creation in the Backyard</i> is McCartney's most recent top-ten album as of 2012<sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Paul_McCartney&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>. It reached number 10 in the UK, and number 6 in the US. It was supported by a UK top-twenty hit single, his most recent as of 2014<sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Paul_McCartney&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, "<a href="/wiki/Fine_Line" title="Fine Line">Fine Line</a>", which failed to chart in the US, and "<a href="/wiki/Jenny_Wren" title="Jenny Wren">Jenny Wren</a>", which reached number 22 in the UK.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-216"><a href="#cite_note-216"><span>[</span>176<span>]</span></a></sup></span></li>
<li id="cite_note-219"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-219">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">McCartney followed the release of <i>Chaos and Creation in the Backyard</i> with <a href="/wiki/The_%27US%27_Tour" title="The 'US' Tour">the 'US' Tour</a>, the tenth top earning act of 2005 in the US, taking in over $17 million in ticket sales for eight shows. During the opening performance of the tour, he played thirty-five songs, of which twenty-three were Beatles tracks.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-218"><a href="#cite_note-218"><span>[</span>177<span>]</span></a></sup></span></li>
<li id="cite_note-221"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-221">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><i>Ecce Cor Meum</i> reached number 2 on the classical charts in both the UK and the US.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBlaney2007276_220-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBlaney2007276-220"><span>[</span>178<span>]</span></a></sup></span></li>
<li id="cite_note-224"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-224">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><i>Memory Almost Full</i> reached number 3 in the US and spending fifteen weeks in the charts. As of 2014<sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Paul_McCartney&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, it remains McCartney's most recent top-five album.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-223"><a href="#cite_note-223"><span>[</span>180<span>]</span></a></sup></span></li>
<li id="cite_note-227"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-227">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><i>Electric Arguments</i> reached number 67 on the <i>Billboad 200</i> and number 1 on the Independent Albums chart.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-226"><a href="#cite_note-226"><span>[</span>182<span>]</span></a></sup></span></li>
<li id="cite_note-234"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-234">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">In November 2010, <a href="/wiki/ITunes" title="ITunes">iTunes</a> made available the official canon of thirteen Beatles studio albums, <i>Past Masters</i> and the <i><a href="/wiki/1962%E2%80%931966" title="1962–1966">1962–1966</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/1967%E2%80%931970" title="1967–1970">1967–1970</a></i> greatest-hits compilations, making the group among the last of the seminal <a href="/wiki/Classic_rock" title="Classic rock">classic rock</a> artists to offer their music for sale on the digital marketplace.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-233"><a href="#cite_note-233"><span>[</span>188<span>]</span></a></sup></span></li>
<li id="cite_note-241"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-241">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">McCartney's band performed thirty-seven songs during 8 May 2012, performance in Mexico City, twenty-three of which were Beatles tracks.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-240"><a href="#cite_note-240"><span>[</span>194<span>]</span></a></sup></span></li>
<li id="cite_note-435"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-435">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">As of 2012<sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Paul_McCartney&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, Elvis Presley has achieved the most UK number-ones as a solo artist with eighteen.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERoberts2005398.E2.80.93400_434-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERoberts2005398.E2.80.93400-434"><span>[</span>387<span>]</span></a></sup></span></li>
<li id="cite_note-441"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-441">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">"Hey Jude" was covered by several prominent artists, including <a href="/wiki/Elvis_Presley" title="Elvis Presley">Elvis Presley</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bing_Crosby" title="Bing Crosby">Bing Crosby</a>, <a href="/wiki/Count_Basie" title="Count Basie">Count Basie</a> and <a href="/wiki/Wilson_Pickett" title="Wilson Pickett">Wilson Pickett</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHarry2000a516.E2.80.93518_440-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHarry2000a516.E2.80.93518-440"><span>[</span>392<span>]</span></a></sup></span></li>
</ol>
</div>
